Commentary

How to Eliminate Foreign News Agencies

— Star

At this critical stage of national crisis, when foreign news agencies are wantonly creating rumors, the press is either actively unable to exert the power of public opinion, or passively unable to prevent the spread of rumors. The mental anguish is extreme. Recently, the Japanese Domei News Agency formally merged with the Denpō News Agency. Their country's news organization has been absolutely unified, and their government can absolutely control it. However, within a week of the merger, they created a rumor that shocked the world, saying that the Guangdong and Guangxi authorities had special actions against the central government. Foreign newspapers in Shanghai rushed to publish it, disturbing people's minds and shaking the financial markets. Only after a day did it become clear that they had been deceived by the Japanese news agency. The maliciousness of the Japanese news agency is deeply regrettable, but the excessive restrictions on the records of our own newspapers and the excessive indulgence of the government towards foreign newspapers and news agencies are also the main causes of such unfortunate events.

The reason why foreign news agencies and foreign newspapers have the ability to spread rumors, and why the readers of our newspapers can be deceived by them, is not a matter of a day or two. Since the government implemented strict censorship, those who care about national affairs have not been able to obtain detailed and important records in Chinese newspapers. Therefore, they quench their thirst with poison and seek them in newspapers run by foreigners. There is a reason why the sales of certain Chinese-language foreign newspapers have increased sharply. The average reader does not understand the source of various news, nor does he consider the background of newspapers and news agencies. When there is shocking news that is not available in domestic newspapers, they immediately believe it to be true. Domestic newspapers know it to be true but do not publish it. In the eyes of readers, this is suspected to be the result of government censorship. Therefore, the false is believed to be true, and the true is suspected to be false. If domestic newspapers have always had complete freedom of recording, this kind of abnormal psychology of readers would not occur.

Secondly, in this extraordinary situation, a considerable degree of news control is not unnecessary. However, once control is implemented, it must be effective. Under the current situation, there are too many loopholes, and the government is overly preferential towards foreign newspapers and news agencies. The Japanese news agency relies on the support of its government and is not subject to censorship. All kinds of outrageous behaviors are commonplace. Even Reuters and Havas and other agencies also enjoy excessive freedom and cannot be brought to justice. Apart from Domei, other foreign news agencies, although not maliciously creating rumors, always take the interests of their own country as a prerequisite when sending a telegram or transmitting a letter, and promote the policies of their country and the reputation of various financial and commercial institutions. When there is a conflict with China's interests, China's interests must be sacrificed. Even if they are subject to mild censorship, they still grumble incessantly. Foreign newspapers are even more unscrupulous, with Japan being the worst and Britain and the United States next. If we want to achieve the actual effect of news control, this is the biggest problem.

Recently, Mr. Ding Bolie, a reporter for the Manchester Guardian stationed in Peiping, published an article in the Pacific Quarterly this month, complaining about the Chinese government's censorship of foreign correspondents' telegrams. However, Mr. Ding also firmly believes that foreign news agencies have strong subjective colors, and cites Japanese news agencies as an example. Mr. Ding also said that the official and semi-official news agencies such as Havas, Oceanic, TASS, and Reuters cannot avoid the color of the official arena and cannot fulfill the responsibility of objectively recording facts. Foreign news agency reporters admit this, so it is by no means excessive for the government to impose stricter controls.

Therefore, giving relatively full freedom of recording to domestic newspapers and imposing strict censorship and control on foreign news agencies and foreign-run newspapers is the urgent task of the government today.

Leith-Ross and Isoya Discuss China's New Currency System, Claiming Assisting China's Economic Revival Benefits All Countries, Isoya Replies that Japan Cannot Agree

(Tokyo) Sir Leith-Ross met with Director of the Military Affairs Bureau Isoya at the British Embassy at 4:00 PM today for about 30 minutes, exchanging important opinions. (8th, Domei News Agency)

(Tokyo) Sir Leith-Ross, the economic advisor to the British government, had a frank discussion with Lieutenant General Isoya, the Director of the Military Affairs Bureau of the Japanese Army Ministry and former military attaché to the Japanese Embassy in China, for two hours today regarding the relationship between Britain and Japan. Sir Leith-Ross expressed his opinion, saying that the Nanjing government should now be regarded as the most complete and powerful political organ in China. For this reason, providing financial assistance to the Nanjing government, enabling it to engage in economic revival and assisting it in building a good national administration, can greatly benefit the stability of the overall situation in China and open the way to maintaining peace in the Far East. He was particularly puzzled by Japan's attitude of not agreeing with the Nanjing government's financial reform plan. It is heard that Lieutenant General Isoya also expressed his personal opinion, saying that Japan is willing to assist China in economic revival, but because Japan has suffered painful experiences in the past, it is currently inconvenient to do so. Japan has close relations with China, so his current position does not allow him to consider providing economic assistance to the Nanjing government. Britain can implement its policies in China on a purely economic basis. (8th, Reuters)

(Tokyo) Sir Leith-Ross, who was in Hakone, entered Tokyo on the morning of the 8th and went to the British Embassy. It was decided that he would visit Foreign Minister Arita at the Ministry of Foreign Affairs on the afternoon of the 9th, as previously arranged, to exchange important opinions regarding the coordination between Britain and Japan. Foreign Minister Arita entrusted Sir Leith-Ross, who was on his way home, to make the British government and people aware of the true meaning of Japan's East Asia policy in order to promote the practical coordination between Britain and Japan. The cautious attitude of the empire has been decided. Therefore, not to mention the three different attitudes towards China in North China, Central China, and Southwest China, the empire will also frankly explain the attitude of the imperial government regarding how China and Japan should implement cooperation to determine the destiny of East Asia, and request Britain's goodwill assistance, and explain that since Britain recognizes Japan's position in China, there is a fundamental principle for Anglo-Japanese coordination. Although Foreign Minister Arita did not attend the welcome lunch for Ross at the British Embassy at noon on the 8th, Horinouchi, a decision-making official, attended on behalf of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs. (8th, Domei News Agency)

(Tokyo) Leith-Ross arrived in Tokyo from Hakone on the morning of the 8th and plans to stay in Tokyo for six days, meeting with Foreign Minister Arita and other government officials and civilians related to China to conduct important discussions. Ross plans to meet with the Foreign Minister first, and then with the military, finance, and industry authorities. Britain's traditional diplomatic policy has always been based on the principle of focusing on the local situation. Ross has been in China for half a year and knows the situation in China well. The significance of his decision to come to Japan again is extremely important. Ross met with former Foreign Minister Hirota last September and proposed the issue of financial assistance to China. In October, he proposed the same loan proposal to China. What proposals he will make when he meets with the Japanese authorities is the most watched thing by the general public. Foreign Minister Arita plans to hold a welcome party for Ross on the evening of the 11th. (8th, Domei News Agency)

Shih Chao-chi Advocates Convening an International Conference

To Resolve the Current Situation Anew, in Order to Avoid War

Durham. Dr. Shih Chao-chi, the Chinese Ambassador to the United States, today received an honorary Doctor of Laws degree from Duke University and addressed the school's graduation ceremony, stating that if the countries of the world wish to avoid war, they should establish a new system of collective peace outside the scope of the League of Nations. Countries should convene an international conference to discuss issues concerning territory and other matters worldwide. The League of Nations has now lost its true power, and China has also recognized that it cannot uphold justice. He also said that if countries wish to avoid war, the major powers should convene a special world conference outside the League of Nations to discuss the redistribution of territories and other important issues. Countries in the East and West should participate in the conference, because the interests of all countries are inseparable. Shih also said that world peace today is in imminent danger, and the reason for this is territorial and other political issues. The League of Nations is only a tool for maintaining the status quo. Therefore, in order to eliminate the problems of territorial and population distribution and the shortcomings of current treaties, an international conference should be convened outside the scope of the League of Nations to seek a solution, and a new international agreement should be established based on the policies of self-preservation and coexistence, so as to promote international mutual benefit and cooperation. Shih also said that although this matter is extremely difficult, it is the only way to avoid war. (7th, Kuomin News Agency)

Branches Established in Various Countries

Australia Increases Tariffs, Japan's Protest Ineffective

Will Retaliation Be Implemented?

Melbourne. After the Australian government received a warning from the Japanese government on the 3rd regarding the invocation of the Trade Protection Act, it held an emergency cabinet meeting and urgently reviewed countermeasures. Prime Minister Lyons, who was on a tour of Tasmania, was contacted by long-distance telephone. After careful consultation, it was decided to maintain the new tariff system and formally responded to Consul-General Murai on the 6th, while expressing hope for effective handling. The main points are as follows: The realization of increased tariffs and import permit systems is not intended to prevent Japanese goods, but only as a means to protect domestic industries. Therefore, even after the implementation of the new system, half of the Australian rayon market and most of the cotton product market remain open to Japanese goods. Although the Australian government does not protest against the changes in tariffs on Australian goods by the Japanese government, the Australian government's decision on the new tariff structure is not aimed at Japanese goods. Therefore, it insists on the new structure from beginning to end, but if an effective solution can be obtained between the Australian government and the Japanese government, the Australian government also hopes for this solution. (8th, Domei News Agency)

Already Arrived in Los Angeles from New York

Los Angeles. Captain Ike, a U.S. Army pilot, departed from New York in a small pursuit plane at 12:15 PM on Wednesday to make the first transcontinental "blind" flight. U.S. Republican Party National Convention

To Convene Today to Nominate Presidential Candidates

Cleveland. The Republican National Convention will convene here on Tuesday, hoping to unite the forces of the moderate faction of the party, formulate a party platform sufficient to appeal to the national public, and nominate presidential and vice-presidential candidates to engage in the general election on November 3. To achieve this goal, the biggest task of the Republican Party at present is to eliminate divergent opinions within the party and launch a united attack on the Democratic Party, which currently controls the White House and both houses of Congress. Therefore, the convention must be able to reconcile the views of the agricultural part of the Midwest with those of the financial and industrial parts. In recent months, the Republican Party has indeed made every effort to put forward a leader sufficient to appeal to the whole country as a presidential candidate, and to adjust the interests of agriculture and industry within the scope of not harming the government's financial and industrial policies. The Republicans in the East are more conservative, and those in the West are more liberal, but which should be the keynote should be decided by the convention. After the convention convenes on Tuesday, all important speeches will be broadcast across the country via radio. The first task will be to elect a temporary chairman, followed by welcome speeches. The standing organization will appear on the second day. In the evening, there may be speeches on policy to declare the party's hopes and guidance. At the same time, various proposals will be submitted. The platform committee will also begin work. Because there are many candidates for this election, the voting will take place at least on Thursday. If the first vote does not produce any results, a second vote will be taken. In the Democratic Party, a candidate must obtain a two-thirds majority to be elected, but in the Republican Party, an ordinary majority can be elected. The length of the session will depend on whether the initial vote can produce a presidential candidate. If Landon can win a majority of votes after one or two votes, the convention can be closed within one or two weeks. If Landon cannot be elected immediately, the meeting will be extended to wait for the presidential candidate to be nominated. (8th, Kuomin News Agency)

Cleveland. It is said that Senator Vandenberg is unwilling to support Landon, and his intention is to reduce Landon's momentum. It is generally believed that if Landon is in a stalemate with the opposition, Vandenberg has a great chance to rise and replace him. (7th, Kuomin News Agency)

Heads of the Little Entente Three Countries Agree on a United Policy

Will Not Hesitate to Use Force Against Changes to the Status Quo

Romanian Capital. King Carol of Romania, Prince Paul of Yugoslavia, and President Benes of Czechoslovakia will each lead their foreign ministers to a meeting at a certain residence near here. It is a historical first for the heads of state of the Little Entente countries to personally discuss important European issues together. The meeting will be held in private. The three countries have firmly stated that the Little Entente countries are united, loyal to the League of Nations, and maintain the dignity of the treaty. (8th, Reuters)

Romanian Capital. King Carol, First Regent Prince Paul of Yugoslavia, and President Benes of Czechoslovakia held their first political meeting at noon today. It was decided that the policy announced by the foreign ministers of the Little Entente three countries on August 5 last year will continue to be adhered to. This policy includes: 1. Opposition to the restoration of the Habsburg royal family. 2. The Little Entente three countries will use force against anyone who attempts to modify the current borders of the Danube River Basin. In addition, the three heads of state also decided to adopt the same attitude as Britain and France on the Locarno case. On the Italo-Ethiopian dispute, the three countries will abide by the resolution of the League of Nations and do not intend to initiate anything. Regarding the reform of the League of Nations, any method that hinders the principle of equality among countries will be firmly opposed by the Little Entente three countries. (6th, Svaha)

Tragedy Occurs at Romanian Military Parade

Grandstand Collapses, Over One Hundred Casualties

Romanian Capital. Today, the 6th anniversary of the restoration of King Carol of Romania was celebrated. While the king was inspecting a parade of 25,000 boy and girl scouts, a large grandstand suddenly collapsed, with hundreds of people on it. After the incident, 14 were found dead and 184 injured. Prince Paul of Yugoslavia and President Benes of Czechoslovakia were also present at the king's inspection. They came here specifically to discuss important European issues. After the disaster, the king also assisted in the rescue. (8th, Reuters)

Romanian Capital. Regarding the collapse of the grandstand during the military parade, it is reported that the first incident was a small grandstand, and several people were slightly injured. Then, a large grandstand also collapsed one after another due to the gathering of thousands of spectators. At least ten bodies have been recovered, and there are more than two hundred injured. All ambulances in the capital have been dispatched to serve. (8th, Havas)

Part of Edinburgh University Students Plan to Elect the Emperor of Abyssinia as President

(London) Part of the students at Edinburgh University are now campaigning to nominate the Emperor of Abyssinia as a candidate for president to replace the late Earl of Airlie. Today, a student told a Reuters reporter that if we can persuade the Emperor to accept this position, it would be an innovation for a head of state to take this position. The Emperor is planning to leave Britain in a week or two, and will go to Switzerland, but will not personally attend the next meeting of the Executive Council of the League of Nations, but will attend as a representative. (7th, Reuters)

(London) A spokesman for the Abyssinian Embassy in London recently announced to the press that the Emperor of Abyssinia will leave for Switzerland in a week or two, but does not intend to personally attend the meeting of the Executive Council of the League of Nations. (7th, Havas)

Belgian Envoy Returns to Peiping from Shanghai

British Emperor's Birthday, Peiping Embassy Suspends Celebrations

(Peiping) June 23 is the 41st birthday of British Emperor Edward VIII. In previous years, the Peiping Embassy has invited the diplomatic corps to celebrate the British Emperor's birthday. This year, due to the national mourning for former Emperor George V, the government has ordered the suspension of celebrations and notified British consulates in various places. (8th, Central News Agency)

Resolution of the French Labor Strike: Workers Achieve Complete Victory, Implementing a 40-Hour Workweek, with Wage Increases of 7 to 15 Percent; 600,000 Workers to Resume Work Imminently

(Paris) French capitalists, under pressure from Prime Minister Blum, have succumbed to the nationwide labor strike and are willing to make concessions. At today's meeting between labor and management, chaired by Blum, the capitalists have agreed to adopt the following measures: widespread wage increases, recognition of labor unions, and permission for collective bargaining. The government is now quite optimistic that the strike movement can be halted by Monday or Tuesday. The workers' only remaining demand, paid holidays, has not yet been accepted. Blum has drafted a bill for a 40-hour workweek, which is likely to be passed by parliament before the end of next week. The issue of paid holidays has also been allowed to be submitted to parliament for discussion. Meanwhile, right-wing elements continue to attack Blum, calling him "the beginning of Jews ruling over the Gauls and Romans." The government has retaliated, seizing a special edition of the reactionary royalist newspaper "French United News" today, due to a scathing article opposing the government. The publisher and editor may also be prosecuted. (National Telegraph, 7th)

(Paris) Regarding the resolution of the labor strike, representatives from the United General Confederation of Labor and the Employers' Federation met for five hours yesterday afternoon, continuing into the night until 1:00 AM this morning, when they signed an agreement. The agreement stipulates the following points: Regarding the right of workers to join labor unions; Regarding the right of workers in various factories and workshops to elect representatives (to liaise with employers on all matters); Regarding the conditions for resuming work in various factories; Regarding the implementation of a 40-hour workweek; Regarding the method of paying wages for one week of annual vacation; Regarding the signing of work contracts by union representatives on behalf of workers with employers. As for wage increases, it is stipulated that senior employees will receive a 7% increase, and junior employees will receive a 15% increase. In addition, factory owners will not pursue any action against striking workers. Although this agreement still needs to be approved separately by local and industry-specific labor unions, factories should resume work as soon as preparations are complete. Interior Minister Salengro, after the signing of the agreement, made a statement to the press, saying, in brief, that approximately 300,000 people joined the strike in the north and 250,000 in the capital. Now that mediation has been successful, the labor strike can be completely ended within 48 hours, which is truly gratifying. The General Confederation of Labor Secretary-General Stone is also satisfied with the end of the labor strike. However, department stores have not joined the Employers' Federation, so the agreement established last night does not include that industry. Interior Minister Salengro has scheduled a meeting this afternoon at the ministry, convening labor and management from that industry to discuss solutions to the disputes, in order to sign a separate agreement. (Havas Dispatch, 8th)

(Paris) Representatives from the United General Confederation of Labor and the Employers' Federation signed an agreement last night, bringing the ten-day-long labor strike to an end. Additional details on yesterday's events are provided below:

Earlier, Prime Minister Léon Blum, yesterday morning, requested that the United General Confederation of Labor and the Employers' Federation each send representatives to immediately begin negotiations to seek conditions for resuming work. Both parties accepted. In the afternoon, negotiations were held at the Ministry of the Interior, chaired by Prime Minister Léon Blum and Interior Minister Salengro. Representing the employers were Dusemin, Chairman of the French Industrial Federation, Liepu, Secretary-General of the Iron Industry Association, the Chairman of the Metallurgical Industry Association, and the Chairman of the Paris Chamber of Commerce. Representing the General Confederation of Labor was Secretary-General Stone and three union representatives. Prior to this, the employers had, in principle, agreed to the two demands made by the labor side: determining the minimum wage and having the work contract signed by the labor union. By 6:00 PM, the negotiations ended. Interior Minister Salengro made a statement to reporters, saying in brief, "A solution to the labor strike has been discussed. However, the representatives of both labor and management must consult with the respective groups they represent. Therefore, the details cannot be released at this time, in order to avoid hindering the progress of negotiations. But I dare to believe that when the representatives of both parties resume negotiations at 11:30 PM, an agreement can be signed, and the labor strikes in various industries will all come to an end." At the same time, the Standing Committee of the United General Confederation of Labor also held a meeting. After the meeting, Secretary-General Stone made a statement to reporters, saying, "After the representatives of labor and management held negotiations at the Ministry of the Interior in the afternoon, a compromise has been reached in principle. However, the representatives of both parties still need to seek the consent of the groups they represent. This was accepted at the meeting of the Standing Committee of the General Confederation of Labor just now. Therefore, both parties should be willing to sign an agreement, as we hope." By 11:30 PM last night, labor and management continued their meeting at the Ministry of the Interior, and an agreement was signed immediately. It was already midnight. (Havas Dispatch, 8th)

(Paris) The labor strike situation improved greatly yesterday. After the Employers' Federation and the United General Confederation of Labor signed an agreement last night, it improved even more. Today is the thirteenth day since the outbreak of the labor strike. Looking at the situation in the capital, the saying of improvement has been clearly confirmed. From this morning, the supply of food for the people has been continuous, no different from normal days. Various public utilities, such as buses, trams, subways, and taxis, have all resumed normal operation. There are no strikes in the banks. Because the Hachette newspaper delivery company has not yet resumed work, the newspapers are temporarily being distributed by the newspaper offices to subscribers in the capital and provinces. However, the labor and management of the delivery company should reach a compromise by tomorrow morning. In several buildings and shops, there are still a small number of workers who have stopped working. As for the metallurgical industry, the strike situation in most factories will not improve until this afternoon. For example, the workers of the Landot and Citroën automobile factories are still occupying the factories and refusing to leave. However, both labor and management believe that the dispute can be resolved, so as to resume work as soon as possible. (Havas Dispatch, 8th)

(Paris) The sit-down strike movement, involving more than 500,000 workers, has now reached a resolution through negotiations between representatives of labor and management at midnight. The representatives of both parties met in the office of the new Prime Minister Blum, with Blum mediating. From yesterday afternoon until late at night, a partial compromise was reached on three points: wage increases, recognition of labor unions, and recognition of factory committees. The employers' representatives insisted that the strikers should immediately return to work, but it was not until midnight that the labor representatives agreed to end the strike after the workers had consulted among themselves. However, the Paris construction industry, without waiting for the results of the labor-management meeting, has decided to strike today. The labor strike resolution agreement stipulates wage increases ranging from 7 to 15 percent, a 40-hour workweek, paid holidays, and collective contracts. It is now expected that the strike will be calmed down within 48 hours. The new government's efforts to mediate the labor strike are seen by the public as a victory for Blum, as Blum took on the arduous task in the first hour of his term. Last night, the Interior Minister announced that the number of strikers was 300,000 in Paris and 250,000 in the northern provinces. It is said that the employers' representatives were forced to make concessions to the labor representatives and accept the labor side's conditions because the new government decided that if a settlement could not be reached, the authorities would intervene. However, because these conditions have economic consequences, they are subject to reservations. The agreement does not apply to large department stores, because these stores have not joined the Employers' Federation. However, the owners and employees of these stores will meet under the supervision of the Interior Minister in the afternoon to resolve their disputes. The new Prime Minister Blum told a Reuters reporter today that he was extremely satisfied with the outcome of the meeting. Labor representative Yoyou also told a Reuters reporter that the agreement reached this time has fulfilled the long-cherished wishes of the workers and has put France on the path to a new economic system. When the House of Representatives meets tomorrow, the government will propose the necessary bills to complete the resolution of the labor strike. (Reuters Dispatch, 8th)

Roubaix, Northern France. The strike has now spread to the textile and related industries of the northern province, and is about to become a general strike. There are as many as 70,000 strikers in the cities of Roubaix and Tourcoing. Except for female workers and child laborers under the age of 15, no one is allowed to leave the factory. (Havas Dispatch, 8th)

Arras, Northern France. A general strike in the coal mining areas of Douai, Lens, and Arras is underway. 150,000 miners and surface workers have occupied the mines and factory buildings, and are changing shifts and taking turns maintaining various equipment inside and outside the mine, without any accidents occurring. The striking workers are under the control of the labor unions of the Northern and Pas-de-Calais provinces and are able to abide by discipline. Representatives of the unions are scheduled to hold talks with representatives of the mine owners' committee tomorrow. (Havas Dispatch, 8th)

Valenciennes. 15,000 metallurgical workers here are on strike, occupying 70 factories. A solution has been negotiated with the employers and work may resume soon. Nice. The famous Blue Train did not run last night because the sleeping car workers joined the strike movement. This is the first time in the history of the railway. (Reuters Dispatch, 8th)

French North Africa Algiers. 6,000 Muslims in the colony of Algeria held a general assembly today and passed a motion making three demands to the French Popular Front cabinet: Algerian Muslims should enjoy all the rights of French citizens, while their original legal status should be maintained; Arab Muslims should be able to elect representatives to join the French parliament; Muslims should be able to establish private schools with Arabic as the official language, and mosques should be free to hold religious ceremonies. (Havas Dispatch, 8th)

New Initiatives of the French Government: Diplomacy and Finance Begin to Be Addressed

(Paris) Foreign Minister Delbos met with the ambassadors to Italy, Chamberlain, and to Germany, Poncet, this morning, and discussed the issues of Abyssinia and the Locarno Treaty, hoping to gather opinions from all parties before the meetings of the League of Nations Council and Assembly. (Havas Dispatch, 8th)

(Paris) Finance Minister Olivo met with the President of the Bank of France, Raberi, and Honorary President Danali, to seek their opinions on the current state of the bank and monetary issues. (Havas Dispatch, 8th)

(Paris) The Figaro newspaper's London correspondent learned that the British Foreign Office, now that the League of Nations Council and Assembly are about to meet and a new French cabinet has been formed, urgently needs to understand what stance the French government will take on the various issues to be discussed at the Geneva Conference, and intends to ask the new French cabinet to provide detailed explanations for reference. The correspondent also said, "It is rumored in London that when French Prime Minister Léon Blum, Foreign Minister Delbos, Ambassador to the UK Corbin, and Secretary-General of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs Rey held talks yesterday, they discussed whether Prime Minister Léon Blum should meet with British Foreign Secretary Eden to study the sanctions issue in detail." (Havas Dispatch, 8th)

Arabs Dig Trenches to Attack Jews: British Troops and Police Rush to Suppress, Several People Killed and Injured After Fierce Fighting

(London) According to today's news in the London News Chronicle, 600 British troops, assisted by police, engaged in a fierce battle with 500 armed Arabs on the small hills along the road from Jerusalem to Jaffa. The trenches dug by the Arabs were the same as the trenches of the Turks during the European War. They were finally defeated by the British troops, and the two villages where they lived were also surrounded by the British troops. (National Telegraph, 7th)

Jerusalem. Arabs dug Turkish-style trenches on the hilltop here and ambushed public buses carrying Jews. Last night, a team of British soldiers, assisted by armed police, attacked the area. A fierce battle ensued for a long time, and searchlights and torches were used to illuminate the battlefield. One British soldier was injured. The number of Arab deaths and injuries is not yet known. It is believed that there must be several people seriously injured. (Reuters Dispatch, 8th)

Jerusalem. A bomb exploded near Jaffa Gate today, injuring seventeen people, mostly Arab farmers. It has not yet been determined who threw the bomb. (Reuters Dispatch, 8th)

Jerusalem City. According to information obtained by this agency's special correspondent, the situation here is becoming increasingly serious. Rumors are circulating that the authorities are planning to declare martial law soon, now that reinforcements have arrived. However, this information has not yet been confirmed. Several Arab leaders, especially Abdul-Lutif, secretary of the Arab Higher Committee, have been arrested. Yesterday, several Arabs attempted to attack Jews and were suppressed by British troops and police. As a result, one person on the side of the military police was injured and three Arabs were killed. A meeting originally scheduled to be held by the Arab mayors today has been banned by the authorities. However, it is said that the mayors are still planning to find a way to hold a meeting tomorrow. (Havas Dispatch, 8th)

Jerusalem. The deadlock in Palestine has not yet been broken. Hady, secretary of the Arab General Strike Committee, and six other Arab leaders have been arrested and will be deported to concentration camps. The Mayor of Bethlehem issued a warning, saying that if city employees do not immediately return to work, the city council will be dismissed and new councilors will be elected. Yesterday, Abdullah, the Emir of Transjordan, suggested to five members of the Arab General Strike Committee during a luncheon in Amman that they stop the riots while the Royal Commission conducts an on-site investigation. The Arab leaders replied that they could not consider stopping the strike unless the British government agreed to fundamentally change its current policy and stop Jewish immigration. Recently, another large unit of British troops arrived from Egypt to strengthen the security of Palestine. The British troops stationed in Palestine now include six infantry battalions, in addition to tank units, mechanized units, and the air force. (Reuters Dispatch, 8th)

Jerusalem. The Arab strike continues to proceed in a lasting way. Arab merchants have recently established a central cooperative here to sell staple foods to their ethnic group, so that there is no shortage. Most of the Arab women recently issued an appeal to British women's groups, saying that the claims made by the Arabs are reasonable and that the British should recognize them. (Havas Dispatch, 7th)

(Geneva) The League of Nations Mandates Commission is scheduled to meet today to discuss the current situation in British Palestine. The British High Commissioner representative there, Torrance-Theia, will attend and participate. (Havas Dispatch, 8th)

Queen Mary's Return Voyage Fails to Achieve Speed Record

(London) The White Star Line's Queen Mary's attempt to break the transatlantic speed record on her first return voyage was again defeated by dense fog. The ship, carrying 1,855 passengers, was forced to reduce speed for one hour and twenty-nine minutes at night. Yesterday, the ship sailed 679 nautical miles in thirty-three hours, with an average speed of 20.92 knots. It must arrive at Cherbourg Rock by 9:28 PM on Tuesday to seize the record held by the French mail ship Normandie. (Reuters Dispatch, 8th)

Swiss National Defense Budget Rejected by Socialist Party Congress

Zurich, Switzerland. The federal government submitted a national defense budget to parliament in April, totaling 235,000,000 Swiss francs. The Executive Committee of the Socialist Party also expressed its support at the time, but at today's National Congress of the Socialist Party, the proposal was rejected by a vote of 263 to 255. Most members of the Executive Committee have now resigned as a result, but will remain in office until a new committee is elected. The Congress then discussed the issue of currency devaluation, and expressed its opposition by a full quorum vote. (Havas Dispatch, 7th)

Draft of the New Soviet Constitution

(Moscow) According to well-informed sources, the draft of the new Soviet constitution, including the preface, is about 10,000 words long. At the meeting of the Pan-Soviet Congress this autumn, it will be personally submitted for discussion by Communist Party Secretary-General Stalin, who will take this opportunity to deliver an important speech. At that time, reporters from foreign newspapers and members of the diplomatic corps will attend as observers. This will be the first time that Stalin has given a public speech to the foreign press and diplomatic corps. It is said that after the promulgation of the new constitution, foreign nationals in the Soviet Union will no longer have the right to vote or be elected. According to the old rules, foreign workers residing in Russia had the right to vote and be elected. However, in the past two years, the Soviet authorities have often ordered these workers to become Russian citizens, otherwise they must abandon their jobs and return to their home countries. This may be a preparation for the implementation of the new constitution. (Havas Dispatch, 7th)

International Commercial Telegraph

Reuters Special Commodity Market Report, June 8

Gold and Silver

London Gold Price: Firm today, up seven pence to 139 shillings and four pence.

London Silver Bar: The silver market was stable today. Spot and futures prices both rose 0.0625 to 20 pence 0.0625. India made some purchases, while China and the general public sold.

Mountrie Silver Market: Opened steadily, with July futures prices up two pounds to 45.17-45.30, due to better overseas telegrams.

Exchange Rates

US-UK: The London foreign exchange market was mixed today. The price of the pound sterling, in terms of the US dollar, was relatively weak. The opening exchange rate for the US-UK was $5.00625, lower than the closing rate of $5.009375 on Saturday. It continued to fall by one pound within the first hour to $4.99625. There was a reaction at 11:00 AM, with the price at $5.00125, but it then softened again. At 1:00 PM, the price was $4.99125, a net decrease of 2.4375 from Saturday.

Securities

New York: The improvement in the French labor strike has made the New York stock market slightly more cheerful today. The prices of most securities rose, led by steel and railroad stocks. There was slight speculative pressure at 11:00 AM, especially on railroad and oil stocks. Traders were inclined to be bullish. At noon, prices were up from a few points to three pounds from Saturday's close. Steel and railroad stocks rose the most. The New York stock market prices are listed below:

Cotton and Wheat

Liverpool Wheat Market: Opened weak due to weak overseas telegrams at the end of last week and news of rain in the Canadian provinces. Prices then rose slightly due to the weekly shipping figures being favorable to the bulls, but prices fell again due to the actual increase in local inventories. At 1:00 PM, the July futures price was 5 shillings 7 pence 375, down one penny 375 from Saturday's close.

Liverpool Cotton Market: The prices for the cotton market were stable today, At 1:00 PM, the July future rose by two points to 6.17 from the fourth.

New York Cotton: The cotton market this morning was still dependent on weather news. Opening prices fell slightly due to reports of rain in the eastern cotton-growing areas, but prices stabilized later due to a firm securities market. At noon, the October futures price was 10.84, up one pound from Saturday's close.

Chicago Wheat Market: Futures were relatively weak this morning due to news of heavy rain in the northwest and across the Canadian wheat area. Trade demand was offset by bullish liquidations. At noon, the September futures price was 84.375, down half a point from Saturday's close. The coarse grains market was strong, with prices rising slightly along with the securities market.

Rubber

London: The rubber market was stable today. At 1:00 PM, the transaction price for July and September futures was 7 pence 375, up 0.0625 from Saturday's close.

New York: The rubber market was firm due to industry buying caused by the gradual improvement in the French labor strike. Opening prices were stable, with September futures up five pounds from the last close to 15.81. Prices rose to 15.89 at noon, a net increase of thirteen pounds from Saturday's close. Chiang Ting-fu and Tao Lyu-qian Arrive in Chongqing to Attend the Sichuan-Guizhou Commissioners Conference

(Chongqing) Chiang Ting-fu and Tao Lyu-qian arrived in Chongqing at 2:00 PM on the 8th by China Aviation flight. Gu Zhutong's representatives Luo Junqiang, Deng Mingjie, Li Hongkun, Zhang Rui, and Wu Jingchao all welcomed them at the airport. Chiang and Tao came to attend the Sichuan-Guizhou Commissioners' Conference and give speeches. According to Chiang, they will stay in Sichuan for about a week for the commissioners' meeting, and then visit Chengdu before returning to Nanjing. The rumors about changes in the southwest are absolutely untrue. The central government's internal and external policies remain consistent and there is absolutely no preparation for using force internally. The rumors that the Guangxi army has entered Hunan are also not true. I met with the Secretary-General of the Hunan Provincial Government last night in Nanjing, and according to him, this statement is completely fictitious. (Central News Agency Dispatch, 8th)

(Nanjing) Chiang Ting-fu flew to Chongqing by plane on the morning of the 8th to attend the Sichuan-Guizhou Commissioners' Conference, to deliver a speech on behalf of President Chiang, and will return to Nanjing after giving an academic lecture at the invitation of Ren Hongjun. (Central News Agency Dispatch, 8th)

(Nanjing) Tao Lyu-qian flew to Chongqing by plane at 9:00 AM on the 8th to attend the Sichuan-Guizhou Administrative Commissioners' Conference and give a lecture. He will return to Nanjing after the meeting. (Central News Agency Dispatch, 8th)

The Legislative Yuan Plans to Amend Regulations on Trade Associations to Enforce Strict Organization and Stop Smuggling

(Nanjing) The Legislative Yuan's Commerce Law Committee has expressed strong support for proposals from various locations to negotiate and stop smuggling, to collectively refuse smuggled goods, and to strictly organize trade associations. Following research, it has already amended the regulations of the Trade Association Law regarding "regulations for sanctions against companies and firms that do not join trade associations." The committee is scheduled to meet at 2:00 PM on the 12th to review the amendment and has sent a letter to the Ministry of Industry to solicit its opinion. Wu Dingchang has submitted the matter of organizing merchant groups to Counselors Chen Feishi and Chen Yu, and Director Zhang Yi'ou of the Commerce Department for detailed research. They will attend the meeting at the appointed time and present their opinions. (8th Dispatch)

Song Zheyuan Convenes Qin Xiao and Others at His Residence to Discuss Foreign Affairs. Xiao Zhenying Remains in Peiping; Returns to Tianjin Later. Political Affairs are Temporarily Managed by Shi Jisheng. Tianjin Authorities Host Banquet for University Presidents to Exchange Views on Eliminating Student Unrest.

(Peiping) Both sides are considering the Hebei-Chahar issue. Tonight, Song Zheyuan convened Qin Dechun, Xiao Zhenying, and other key figures at his residence for discussions. (8th Dispatch)

(Tianjin) Municipal Government Secretary-General Shi Jisheng, Public Security Bureau Chief Sun Weilian, Security Commander Liu Jialuan, and Social Affairs Bureau Chief Liu Dongxuan hosted a banquet at the Municipal Government's Flower Hall at 6:00 PM on the 8th for the presidents of Tianjin's universities to exchange views on eliminating student unrest and preventing foreign excuses for interference. (8th Dispatch)

(Tianjin) Xiao Zhenying will remain in Peiping to focus on diplomatic efforts with Matsumuro; his return to Tianjin is temporarily postponed. Municipal government affairs will be temporarily managed by Secretary-General Shi Jisheng, effective the 8th. (8th Dispatch)

Smuggled Goods Loaded and Shipped to Chongqing; Chamber of Commerce Discusses Sanctions

(Chongqing) The number of smuggled goods arriving in Chongqing has increased recently, mostly transported by merchant ships from a certain country. The Chongqing Customs has resolved to conduct thorough inspections. The Municipal Chamber of Commerce will hold a meeting today to discuss measures to sanction unscrupulous merchants. (8th Dispatch)

Anhui Provincial Government Orders Investigation into Japanese Warship Collision; Over Forty Passengers Rescued; Japanese Warship Voluntarily Compensates for Losses

(Wuhu) The Japanese warship "Kuri" collided with and sank a ferry crossing the Yangtze River at Digang. Over forty passengers were rescued. The Japanese warship voluntarily compensated for the losses, and the matter has been resolved. The Anhui Provincial Government sent a telegram to Wuhu on the 8th, ordering an investigation into the incident. (8th Dispatch)

Hebei Provincial Bank Expands Scope of Agricultural Loans

(Tianjin) The Hebei Provincial Bank's rural loans have been effective. It now plans to allocate 300,000 yuan to cooperate with the China International Famine Relief Commission's rural cooperation efforts to expand the scope of agricultural loans. (8th Dispatch)

Agricultural Credit Bureau Organization; Country Divided into Five Regions; Board of Directors Set at Twenty-Three Members

(Nanjing) The Agricultural Credit Bureau will be established on July 1st. The organizational regulations were reviewed at a meeting of the Executive Yuan on the 8th without modifications. They are scheduled to be presented for discussion at the Executive Yuan meeting on the 9th. The main points of the regulations are divided into two departments: agricultural production and agricultural resources. The country will be divided into five regions, and its business will be completed within five years. The headquarters will be located in the capital, with branches in major ports. The board of directors will be set at twenty-three members, with a president and vice president appointed from among the directors. The ex officio directors are Kong Xiangxi, Wu Dingchang, Zhang Jia'ao, Jiang Zuobin, Yu Feipeng, Qin Fen, Xu Tinghu, Qian Tianhe, Cai Wuji, etc. (8th Dispatch)

Lu Salt Export; Measures Not Yet Agreed Upon

(Tianjin) Special Commissioner Wu convened a meeting of relevant parties on the 8th to discuss the export of Lu salt. Because the issue of selecting exporters has not been resolved, the Special Commissioner's Office is concerned about the potential for private sales and is proceeding cautiously. However, there will be two routes for future shipments: one from the Beining Railway to Tanggu for transshipment to Japan, and the other from local docks by civilian boats via the Jiyun River to the outer port for transshipment to larger ships. (8th Dispatch)

Tianjin Cigarette Merchants Oppose Tax Increase Dispute

(Tianjin) Regarding the opposition of cigarette merchants to the local collection of consolidated taxes, representatives originally planned to petition on the 8th. However, the government entrusted the trade association to dissuade the cigarette merchants and wait for the Hebei-Chahar Committee's instructions. Currently, all stores have stopped stocking up, and the market will likely experience panic after a week. (8th Dispatch)

(Tianjin) The cigarette industry here is at a standstill due to the local authorities' attempt to levy an inspection tax on cigarettes, which is equivalent to a consolidated tax. The cigarette tax bureau refuses to release any cigarettes that only have the central government stamp but lack proof of payment of the supplementary tax. Chinese merchants are not complying with the new regulations. At the same time, the local authorities are preparing to levy a supplementary tax on egg products. Chinese merchants have stated that these products already pay three types of taxes, and if a supplementary tax is levied, it will be difficult to compete with foreign goods. Therefore, they are requesting the Hebei-Chahar Political Affairs Committee to cancel the above order. (8th Reuters Dispatch)

Qin Fen and Zheng Zhaojing in Hankou; Decide on Flood Control Measures; Xiang Embankment Rehabilitation Committee Organized; Qin Left Hankou Yesterday to Inspect Shagang

(Hankou) Qin Fen, Zheng Zhaojing, Yang Yongtai, Fan Xiji, Liu Shoupeng, and others in Hankou discussed and decided on flood control measures for the Jianghan area and matters related to the rehabilitation of the Xiang embankment. They also finalized the organization of the Xiang Embankment Rehabilitation Committee, which will be divided into three departments: Xi Dejiong will be in charge of general affairs, Chang Yuling will be in charge of transportation, and Chen Ruzhen will be in charge of engineering, all under the command of Fan Xiji. Guangdong Province's Second-Phase Plan Awaiting Review, Approval, and Implementation; Implementation Scheduled to Begin Next Month; Construction Department Submits Entire Plan; Factory Component Expands Existing Facilities

Guangzhou Correspondent: The agencies under the Guangdong Provincial Government have sequentially drafted and submitted the province's second three-year plan. About 70% to 80% of the items have been collected and can be completed within the month. A preliminary summary review will begin. The heads of the Civil Affairs, Finance, Construction, and Education Departments will take the opportunity to jointly inspect the counties in the central region to understand the situation and use it as a basis for conducting group reviews of the plans of each department. This is the most recent change in the procedures for drafting, reviewing, and deciding on the second three-year plan by the provincial government. It has been determined that the joint inspection of the four department heads should be conducted in March, April, May, and June of this year to review and improve the initial three-year plan, assess its administrative achievements, and lay the groundwork for drafting the second-phase plan. However, due to government affairs, the department heads could not spend too much time on inspection. Therefore, it was proposed to conduct the joint inspection of the central region as early as possible. Suddenly, Mr. Hu passed away in Guangzhou, and the trip had to be suspended. Subsequently, representatives from the Central Government arrived in Guangdong to mourn Hu's passing and discuss important matters related to the party and the country. For these reasons, the four department heads and Chairman Lin delayed the inspection of past administrative plans and the progress of drafting the second-phase plan. It has recently been learned that the department heads have decided on the inspection dates again and have tentatively scheduled the inspection itinerary. Provincial Government Chairman Lin Yizhong will still travel to the southern route via the Wuyi area. The three department heads, Qu Fangpu, Huang Linshu, and He Qihong, will jointly inspect the central region. Chairman Lin stated that the 25th year will begin in July, and the province's second three-year plan will be implemented from the 25th year. There is only one month left for preparation, which is urgent. The second-phase plans of the civil affairs, finance, and education departments and other agencies have been drafted and submitted to the provincial government. Only the construction department has not submitted concrete plans, which not only affects the preliminary review work but also has a bearing on the group review and overall decision. Therefore, Construction Department Head He Qihong was ordered to draft and submit the plans to the provincial government for review to revive the economy. As for the provincial government's factories that generate private economic income, the focus is on reorganization, improvement, and increasing production. Constructions that have no major relationship to the national economy will not be included in the plan. The expansion plans for the various provincial government factories are divided into three aspects: output, funds, and management.

- The managers of the provincial government factories are only responsible for planning to increase production and improving the machinery and procedures in the factory.

- The marketing of the products is the sole responsibility of the Provincial Government Product Management Office.

- All income and expenditure of the various factories are managed by the Provincial Government Factory Audit Committee, which will properly use the surplus funds as a reserve for expanding the factories.

Japanese People's Active Conspiracy in Inner Mongolia: Aiming for a Grand Encirclement of the Soviet Union and Outer Mongolia

Since realizing its ambition to annex Manchuria, Japanese imperialism has been eyeing the vast, boundless plains of Siberia. This area is a treasure trove yet to be developed, possessing abundant mineral resources such as coal, iron, and petroleum, all essential resources for national defense. Resource-poor Japan believes that if it can occupy this territory, it can establish an unshakable foundation for dominating East and West Asia. However, Japan's ambition cannot be achieved as easily as the Manchurian Incident, with a simple wave of the hand and a satisfactory success. Since the September 18th Incident, the Soviet Union has stationed over 300,000 elite Red Army troops in its vast territories along the Far Eastern border and has actively strengthened various military facilities, preparing to deliver a head-on blow to invaders. Therefore, Japan dares not act rashly to achieve its goals and must make further preparations in its military deployment. Taking advantage of Inner Mongolia is one of these preparations. It wants to establish a second puppet state in the provinces of Chahar and Suiyuan, advance westward to seize Ningxia, and form a grand encirclement of the Soviet Union and Outer Mongolia, with the aim of invading Outer Mongolia and cutting off the Siberian Railway, attacking Chita, Ulan-Ude, Irkutsk, and other places. Japan's plan to seize Inner Mongolia began after annexing the four northeastern provinces.

At that time, it changed the three leagues of Jerim, Jorosutu, and Jouda into the puppet Xing'an Province, which was a preparation for establishing a puppet Mongolian state in the future. Its methods of operation are twofold: on the one hand, to appease the feudal rulers, and on the other hand, to use traitors to exert pressure. In the past four years, the activities of the Japanese in Bailingmiao, Pangjiang, and Zhangjiakou have all been like this. And the puppet troops such as Li Shou-hsin and Zhuo Shi-hai are rampant in eastern Chahar, and they are plotting to annex the two provinces sooner or later. Now we can point out all the conspiracies and facilities of the Japanese and traitorous puppet troops to remind the people of the country to pay attention. The first is the activity of the puppet troops. Since Li Shou-hsin and Zhuo Shi-hai's puppet troops occupied the six counties of Guyuan, Baochang, Zhangbei, Shangdu, Kangbao, and Huade in eastern Chahar, they have established two military academies in Zhangbei, recruiting a large number of Mongolian youths for training. At the same time, they also took advantage of the serious Mongolian disaster last winter to recruit soldiers on a large scale and expand their strength. Recently, they have further maintained contact with Zhang Hai-peng's puppet troops on the Rehe border and scattered bandits, deciding to take military action to the west. When possible, they will invade Guihua to the south, hoping to complete the first step in encircling Outer Mongolia and the Soviet Union within the provinces of Chahar and Suiyuan.

Secondly, in order to cover up the activities of the puppet troops, the Japanese have sent an air force team of twenty aircraft from outside the Guan, stationed in Zhangbei, Pangjiang, and Bailingmiao, and have opened up a large airfield there. At the same time, wireless radio stations have been set up in Suiyuan, Baotou, and Ningxia to communicate with each other. The third is the anesthetizing work in culture. Now the Japanese have established so-called goodwill associations and good neighbor associations in important places such as Pangjiang, Bailingmiao, and Baotou. The work done by these groups is mostly about charity on the surface, such as free medical treatment and poverty relief, etc. In reality, it is a propaganda machine. They have sent many young Japanese people to organize mobile medical teams to provide free medical treatment in various places, taking the opportunity to spread their absurd theories of Mongolian autonomy. At the same time, they have also established many small schools to implement enslaving education. Geographically speaking, the entire Inner Mongolia is a barrier in the northwest of our country. Now the Japanese are deliberately planning to plunder this land of national defense outposts, which can be used as a base for further encroaching on the Central Plains. Its seriousness is truly no less than that of North China. The people of the country really should not ignore it! (China United News Agency)

Nanking City: Land Registration Situation - Achievements After the Restoration of the Land Bureau - The City-wide General Registration Will Soon Be Completed

Nanking Correspondence: The Nanking Municipal Government, in order to expedite the city-wide general land registration, restored the Land Bureau last July. Since its establishment on July 20 last year, the bureau has made unremitting efforts in land administration. Now the city-wide general registration is about to be completed. In order to clarify the land administration situation in the Nanking City, the work of the City Land Bureau since its establishment is specially explored and recorded as follows:

Registration Situation

Land registration in Nanking City began in July 1934. Although the Land Law had been promulgated at that time, it had not yet been implemented. The municipal government separately formulated the "Provisional Rules for Land Registration in Nanking City" as a guideline for handling matters. The city, Xiaguan, and Pukou, etc., which have been surveyed and cleared, are divided into eight registration districts, and registration applications are requested by district within a time limit. The Land Registration Office of the Finance Bureau is responsible for land registration matters. As of June last year, the deadline for registration applications in the first to sixth districts of the city had all expired. A total of 19,745 ownership registration cases were received, and a total of 2,017 cases were approved for registration. When the Land Bureau was established in July last year, it continued to handle the registration cases in the first to sixth districts, and started land registration in the seventh and eighth districts on September 1 last year, and shortened the application deadline to 40 days. After the deadline, it was found that there were still a large number of business owners in each area who had not registered. If penalties were imposed in accordance with the regulations, or their land was disposed of, citizens would suffer many losses. In order to show consideration for business owners and complete the registration, the government changed the deadline for registration in each district to the end of December 1935, and formulated a presumed registration method. For land that is not registered after the deadline, the Land Bureau will presume registration as ownerless land. If no one claims an objection after the announcement period expires, the bureau will presume to take over the land. After one year, it will be officially taken over as city land. This method, on the one hand, promotes the completion of registration, and on the other hand, still gives citizens the opportunity to restore ownership. As of May 23 this year, the Land Bureau has received a total of 17,429 ownership registration cases and 7,038 other property rights registration cases. The handling of registration cases is statistically listed by district and by month as follows:

Table 1: Statistics on Ownership Registration Cases Handled as of May 23, 1936

"Note" The total number of cases received in the table is 17,429. In addition to the 22,629 cases that have been approved for announcement, there are still 4,800 cases in backlog, including 70 cases that were mistakenly reported for registration outside the scope of the registration district, 150 cases that were suspended from registration within the scope of the political district requisition, 212 cases where property rights disputes have occurred and lawsuits have been filed in court, and registration has been suspended, and 559 cases where duplicate applications and other property rights were mistakenly reported as ownership registration and have been revoked. The above items total 991 cases, so the actual number of ownership registration cases being processed as of May 23 this year is 3,809.

Table 2: Monthly Statistics of Land Registration Cases Handled by the Nanking City Land Bureau (from July 24, 1935 to May 23, 1936)

Registration Procedure

Nanking used to be an important place in Jiangnan and has suffered many wars. Most of the property deeds of the people have been lost. Although several supplements were made at the end of the Qing Dynasty and the beginning of the Republic of China, they were not thoroughly organized, but instead caused more chaos. According to the statistics, there are dozens of types of deeds and certificates found in Nanking City, including those from the Post-War Rehabilitation Bureau, the Agricultural Encouragement Bureau, the Land Reclamation Bureau, the Qing Text Bureau, the Palace Property Bureau, the Commercial Port Bureau, the Camp Property Office, the Police Department, the Military Governor's Office, various municipal bureaus, and other military and political organs, Jiangning Prefecture, Shangyuan County, Jiangning County, and the county finance bureaus and other organs' printed contracts, pawn contracts, as well as new contracts, verification contracts, official contracts, white contracts, verification forms, survey forms, receipts, package agreements, etc. The location, household name, area, and four boundaries of the land recorded are also extremely simple and vague, and the property rights are extremely difficult to determine. Often, there is only one piece of land, and it is bought and sold repeatedly, and there are as many as forty or fifty deeds and certificates. The sizes, lengths, widths, and forms are not uniform, and the heads and tails of the contracts are attached to each other, and they are divided, cut, and continued to be white, broken and fragmented. Insinuations and forgeries make it even more difficult to identify. The purpose of land registration is to organize land. In order to carefully protect property rights, the City Land Bureau strives for detailed procedures. All registration cases should first be filled out by the owner in an application form, and the contract and certificate should be submitted for registration. After checking the base map, investigating the use of the surrounding areas, reviewing the area and houses, and measuring and preparing the review map, the review can begin after all kinds of procedures. During the review, the household name, location, four boundaries, area, surrounding land conditions, rights and interests, and the authenticity and completeness of the documents must be strictly checked. If any doubts arise, investigation, inquiry, or other methods must be used to accurately determine the truth of the property rights. After the review is determined, it will be announced. After the three-month period expires, if no objection is raised, the ownership map will be prepared, sent to the court for printing, and then notified to collect it. Therefore, each registration case takes an average of six months to complete after this cumbersome procedure and approve the registration. If the registration process is hindered because the applicant and interested parties cannot be summoned, or because the relevant documents cannot be verified, the registration process will inevitably be hindered. If a property rights dispute occurs, the review can only be carried out after the court makes a judgment, and the registration will inevitably be delayed. This is the ordinary registration procedure for registration cases.

Registration Fee and Penalties

The registration fee for land registration in Nanking City is collected in accordance with the provisions of the revised "Provisional Rules for Land Registration in Nanking City." It is calculated that for the first ownership registration, a fee of two per thousand is charged according to the declared price or occupancy price. For registration of the acquisition, establishment, transfer, or change of land rights, a fee of one per thousand is charged according to the selling price or the value of the rights. In addition, the book fee is charged for each sheet according to the value of land rights as follows: less than 100 yuan is 20 cents, 100 yuan or more is 50 cents, 500 yuan or more is 1 yuan, 1,000 yuan or more is 2 yuan, 5,000 yuan or more is 5 yuan, 10,000 yuan or more is 10 yuan. As for the registration penalties, it is stipulated that if a land rights holder or obligor requests registration after the registration deadline, an additional registration fee of 4/10 of the fee will be levied for every 15 days overdue. In addition, the presumed registration will be held from 1936, and it is stipulated that those who are approved to make up the registration after the presumed registration is announced shall pay a fine of 5/1000 of the registered property price. The above registration fees and the fees charged for overdue registration, as well as the fines for making up the registration, are all collected by the Land Bureau and submitted to the municipal treasury on a daily basis. It is found that from July 1935 to the end of April 1936, the bureau collected a total of 38,388.02 yuan in registration fees and 95.68 yuan in penalties for overdue registration.

Organization and Expenses

The Nanking City Land Bureau has three sections: the first, second, and third sections. The first section has three groups: general affairs, registration, and land acreage. The second section has a survey group and seven review groups. The third section has two groups: surveying and mapping, and a labor examination group. The surveying group has eight surveying teams. This is a general overview of the bureau's original organizational structure. However, this year, the bureau was ordered to be renamed the Land Administration Bureau, and the organizational rules have been revised. Except for the first and third sections, the second section has added a land tax group to handle land tax matters starting next year. The source of funds for the Land Bureau is provided by the municipal treasury. The bureau's 1935 budget includes 371,568 yuan for recurring expenses and 360,000 yuan for temporary expenses, totaling 751,568 yuan. The amount of temporary expenses is relatively large because the general registration is being actively expedited this year, and the organization and business have expanded, so the temporary expenses have been appropriately increased. The purpose of these temporary expenses is to expedite registration, increase the salaries of staff, office expenses, and purchase surveying instruments. In addition to the fixed monthly payment of salaries and office expenses, the purchase expenses must be submitted to the municipal government for approval when needed. Therefore, the actual temporary expenses paid by the bureau each month are about 8,700 yuan in July 1935 (including start-up expenses), more than 32,000 yuan in August (including the purchase of vehicles, instruments, clothing, and furniture), and an average of about 18,000 yuan per month from September to April 1936, which is about 60% of the budget. This is a general overview of the bureau's expenses.

Suzhou: Farmers in the Suzhou Countryside are Causing Trouble Again

Farmers in Chefang, Xietang and other villages in the Suzhou countryside have continuously engaged in disturbances over rent. The county government, considering that the collection of rent by various firms was not prosperous, ordered the county to collect 50%, while the land tax collection was only about 70%. Therefore, it will set up a mobile grain collection point in Xietang Township within a few days. Unexpectedly, on the morning of the 6th, farmers in Yangmu and Shigang and other places in Xietang Township gathered to cause trouble. After the security team rushed to suppress them, the situation was quickly calmed down. At that time, the farmers who resisted the rent and caused trouble, Hu Shengyuan and others, were arrested and sent to the public security branch for verification. On the morning of the 7th, at about 8:00, about 200 farmers were found gathering in a dilapidated temple in the Duixu area, intending to petition. They were also dispersed by the security team. At about 2:00 in the afternoon of the same day, more than 400 farmers from Lianmu Village and other places took more than a dozen farm boats to the home of Zhao Buqing, a Baowu chief in Xiepo Village, and destroyed the furniture and objects before dispersing. Nie Dezhao, the captain of the security brigade, reported the previous situation and immediately went to the countryside, convened a meeting of the villagers, and persuaded them to do everything. It is said that on the evening of the same day, more than 100 farmers in Jinmiao Township also plotted to cause trouble over rent, but they did not dare to take any action due to the strict defense of the police team. The official department has no fundamental solution to this problem.

Husband Chops and Injures Adulterous Couple

Shen Genshi, a farmer in Xiexing Village, Muqiao Township, discovered that his wife, Xie Jinying, was having an affair with Zhang Quanlin, a villager. At about 4:00 p.m. on the 7th, Shen Yao was out selling silk and returned home. After entering the door, he saw his wife, Xie, and Zhang Quanlin sleeping on the same bed. So, he angrily obtained a kitchen knife and chopped Xie's head several times. Zhang Quanlin, the adulterer, was also chopped several times. After the two were injured, they fell to the ground and could not move. The incident was heard by the neighbors and reported to the fifth branch of the public security bureau, which dispatched the police to arrest Shen Genshi and send him to the branch. At the same time, the injured people were sent to the hospital for treatment. Zhang Quanlin's injuries were quite serious and his life was in danger. On the 8th, the county branch sent Shen Genshi to the public security bureau and then to the district procuratorate for interrogation. It is said that Shen Genshi confessed to the public security bureau that he committed the crime out of anger. Shen Xie also confessed that she had an affair with Zhang Quanlin.

Wuxi: Bumper Fresh Cocoon Harvest

The cocoon firms in the four villages of the county have already started weighing. The volume of goods received on the third day was more enthusiastic than on the first day. Because the farmers were eager to use the money, they had to sell their cocoons at a low price. On the 8th, the volume of goods received by the cocoon firms in the urban area was not prosperous due to the rainy weather. The price of cocoons was 35 yuan higher. The volume of goods received by the cocoon firms in rural areas such as Houtai, Zhi Banqiao, Lishe, Zhangcun, Ludianqiao, Xiajiabian, Huangtutang, Jilangbang, Qingqi, Zhaqiao, Helukou, Shitouwan, Beifangquan, and Kuopu was very large. Each firm could receive one or two hundred loads of goods every day. The price of cocoons was 37 yuan higher, and the price of silk was 35 yuan per load. However, wealthy households generally bake fresh cocoons into dried cocoons and wait for a good price to sell them.

Small Loans for Industry and Commerce

The head office of Jiangsu Bank, regarding the case of providing small loans for industry and commerce, has been instructed by the Jiangsu Provincial Government to approve the case and requested the Jiangsu Higher Court to order the county governments to inform the chambers of commerce in the counties and cities to assist in the handling. The branches and offices of the bank, in addition to the two special municipalities of Shanghai and Nanjing, have the following branches and offices in the counties of the province: (branches) Zhenjiang, Wuxi, Wuxian, Nantong, Changshu, (sub-branches) Wujin, Tongshan, Taixian, Taixing, Donghai, Huaiyin, (offices) Haimen, Qidong, Jingjiang, Jiangpu, Jiangdu, Zhuanyou, Yizheng, Huaian, Xiaoxian, Dangshan, Siyang, etc., a total of 21 places. In order to facilitate management, the head office intends to instruct the branch offices to be responsible for the pilot implementation. If the implementation is successful, it will be gradually promoted. In order to carefully account for the loans, it has specially written to the chambers of commerce to organize a review committee to introduce small loans for industry and commerce. However, the amount of the loan shall not exceed 1,000 yuan of the national currency, and the term shall not exceed four months. Those who breach the contract and fail to repay shall be subject to administrative and legal sanctions by the local government. Merchants or factories that have not joined the same industry association shall not be allowed to apply for loans.

Yangfu Highway to be Completed

The Yangfu Highway between Yangjian Town in this county and Fushan Town in Changshu County was started last month. The earthwork project has been largely completed, and the road surface is now being paved with gravel and cinder. It is expected to be completed by the end of this month. The issue of future traffic will still be handled by the Xihu Company.

Changzhou: Market Conditions After Cocoon Firms Open

A total of 87 cocoon firms have registered and reported to be open in the city and rural areas of Wuyi this year. The opening date was decided by the Cocoon Association to be June 8. However, the cocoon harvest in the southeast villages was earlier, so the cocoon firms in Donghenglin, Weishuyan, Tangqiao, Banshang, Xianjiaqiao, and Chenduqiao and other towns opened successively on June 7 to collect cocoons. The quality of the improved silkworm cocoons is very good. Although the arrival of goods is not very crowded, the price of cocoons has exceeded the expected price. The price of improved silkworm cocoons on the city scale is 35-6 yuan higher per load, and the price of native cocoons is 25-6 yuan. The cocoon harvest in the northwest villages is also started on the 7th, but the arrival of goods is very scarce. From about the 8th, the county's cocoon firms will be in a peak harvest period, and the people are all overjoyed after the price has increased.

Yangzhou: Deadline for Canal Dredging Order from the Department

The Jiangdu County Government, because it had previously received an order from the Construction Department to issue this year's measures for conscripting labor to dredge rivers in various counties, had already transferred the order to the district offices with dredging relations for consultation and handling. Now that the year is coming to an end, it has continued to receive an order from the Construction Department, instructing to complete the dredged rivers by the end of this month, and those that have not been completed shall be rushed to completion by June 15, and reported to the Department for statistics. The order was transferred to the dredging district chiefs on the 6th to comply with.

Nantong: Investigating Smuggling Along the River and Sea

In the coastal areas of the Nantong jurisdiction, there have been frequent cases of treacherous people colluding with Japanese and Korean vagrants to transport smuggled goods in sand boats and unload them from remote ports. The Nantong District Commissioner's Office has ordered the police of the county's water and land public security teams to strictly investigate and crack down on smuggling. The coastal areas are the responsibility of the water public security teams of the three districts.

Jiaxing: Cocoon Firms Stop Weighing Separately

There are more than 50 cocoon firms in Jiaxing this year. The cocoon firms that collect native cocoons have already stopped weighing. The cocoon firms that buy improved silkworm cocoons have been open for nine days. Most of them have started weighing on rest days. Because the goods were crowded this year, the number of each cocoon firm exceeded the original registered amount. Because the cocoon collection time has been extended, after the suppliers stopped weighing, there are still a large number of fresh cocoons in the countryside that are still required to be collected, resulting in disputes. Fortunately, the Weicheng Textile Factory is still buying cocoons, and the nearby villagers mostly carried them to sell, while the villagers in remote areas felt very inconvenient. Therefore, local people telegraphed the Cocoon Collection Committee to find a way to provide relief, but it is unknown how to handle it.

Cixi: Interviewers of the Local History Museum

The Cixi County History has been around for many years. In February, the county government convened people from various villages and decided to revise it.
