Sun Jinxian, a 26-year-old native of Ningbo, works at the Xinhua Dyeing and Weaving Factory at No. 159, Singapore Road, West Shanghai. Yesterday, he went to work at the factory, and he carried dozens of counterfeit jiao notes from the China Farmers' Bank. Gu Xiejie, the factory's accountant, found out and reported it to the Singapore Police Outpost. After receiving the report, the outpost reported it to the chief police, who went and arrested Sun. Twenty-eight counterfeit jiao notes from the China Farmers' Bank were found in Sun's possession on the spot and taken to the outpost. They were transferred to the Caojiadu Public Security Bureau for interrogation. The bureau considered that the case involved the use of counterfeit money and immediately sentenced him to be sent to the General Bureau for interrogation.

Public Concession: Three Robbery Cases in One Day

Route D'affaires (now Huashan Road): Ding Chengrong, a man from Shaoxing, aged 20, lived at 7 Gaozhao Xing Lane, Route D'affaires. He worked as a bill collector for a local newspaper. He had recently set up his own office at his home. Yesterday morning around 7:00 AM, Ding left his house with over 350 yuan in collected funds, intending to deposit it. Unexpectedly, just as he reached the entrance of the lane, three bandits stopped him. They threw a bag of lime powder at his face. Ding, realizing the danger, desperately resisted the bandits. However, he was outnumbered and ultimately defeated. All the funds were stolen. At that moment, Ding was extremely anxious and shouted for help. Nearby patrol officers heard the alarm and rushed to the scene to pursue the bandits. They apprehended one bandit nearby and recovered part of the stolen money on his person. Both were taken to the police station to await trial by the court.

Soochow Creek Road (now Suzhou Creek Road): Zhen Zhi of Anhui province, resided at No. 31, Lane 714, Soochow Creek Road, west of Shanghai. He was a manager at the Yichangsheng Soap Factory. Around 6:00 AM yesterday morning, while the maid was opening the door to prepare water, six bandits suddenly forced their way in, went straight upstairs, woke up Zhen and his family, forbade them from making any noise, and forced them to hand over the keys to the chests. They opened each one and searched and looted everything. After about an hour, they fled. Before leaving, the bandits saw a bicycle downstairs and stole it as well. Afterwards, the victim checked and found that he had lost over 1,000 yuan in cash, foreign currency, and jewelry. He immediately prepared a list of the stolen items and reported it to the Gordon Road Police Station (now Nanjing West Road Police Station), requesting an investigation. The police station immediately dispatched Chinese and foreign detectives to the scene to investigate and will pursue the bandits for trial after they are apprehended.

Pingliang Road: At a residence with the address of No. 366 Pingliang Road, belonging to someone surnamed Mou, four bandits arrived at around 8:40 PM last night to commit a robbery. First, two unarmed bandits tricked their way into opening the main door, then two armed bandits with pistols forced their way into the inner room, confining all the men and women in the house. They then threatened them to hand over valuables. However, the Mou family was not wealthy, so they were only robbed of 86 yuan in cash and fled. The victim reported the incident to the local police station, requesting an investigation.

Weak Will of a Country Woman: A Page in a History of Depravity. Divorced from her husband, she willingly became a mistress. Stealing gold jewelry, she was accused by relatives.

Lin Zuolong, a man from Fujian province, currently working as a wireless radio officer in the Zhengji Shipping Company's Shanghai-Qingdao route, is 30 years old. Two years ago, he married Dan Keqing (also known as Zhaoqiu, 18 years old this year), a woman from his hometown of Fuzhou. After the marriage, Lin came to Shanghai to work, while Dan stayed in the countryside. Last winter, because Lin's cousin, Wang Lin (her husband was the late Wang Jingshun, former liaison section chief of the Shanghai Diplomatic Commissioner's Office), had vacant rooms at No. 34 Taoyuan Village, Route Lafayette (now Fuxing Middle Road) in the French Concession, Lin brought his wife Dan Keqing to Shanghai to stay at Wang's house. Lin himself, due to his work on the ship, entrusted his cousin to take care of his wife. Wang Lin trusted Dan quite a bit, so she gave Dan the key to the iron safe. Unexpectedly, after arriving in Shanghai, Dan became obsessed with cabaret dances. Between January and February of this year, she met Fei Shengxiang, a young man from Wuxi who worked as a pattern maker. They fell in love. Dan often wrote love letters at home to send to Fei, but she never sent them. Instead, she discarded them in the wastepaper basket. Wang Lin found them and hid them in the iron safe. Last month, Lin Zuolong returned to Shanghai and discovered that Dan's behavior was unusual. He gathered matchmakers and witnesses on the 23rd of last month and signed a divorce agreement at a law firm, officially ending their marriage. After the divorce, Dan took all her clothes and other belongings and went with her lover Fei Shengxiang back to Fei's house in Xuejiadu near the Zhoujingxiang train station in Wuxi to live together. However, Fei already had a wife. Only then did she realize that she had been deceived. She had no choice but to endure being a concubine. On the 28th of last month, Wang Lin, Lin Zuolong's cousin, opened the iron safe and found that two love letters and gold jewelry worth 330 yuan were missing. She knew that Dan had stolen them. She reported the theft to the French police station, requesting an investigation. The police station reported to the Second Special District Court, which issued an arrest warrant. Detective Wang Zhongfa went to Wuxi, joined the Public Security Bureau, went to Fei's house in Xuejiadu, arrested Dan Keqing, recovered the stolen goods, and brought her back to Shanghai. Yesterday, she was sent to the 8th Criminal Court of the Second Special District Court. Yuan Jiahuang, a lawyer from the police department, presented the case, accusing her of theft. Xu Wufang, a lawyer representing the plaintiff, stated that the plaintiff's side had already recovered the stolen goods, with very little missing, and they could not avoid pursuing the matter. When questioned, Dan Keqing confessed to the theft, but said that she did not intend to steal, but only to retrieve the love letters. The police department lawyer expressed his opinion, saying that this case was not a crime that required prosecution by the plaintiff, and the plaintiff and the defendant were no longer related. He requested that the court investigate and adjudicate according to the law. Judge Sun Penghuan reviewed the confession and ordered that the debate should begin and then conclude. The court sentenced Dan Keqing to 30 days of detention, suspended for two years, and ordered the stolen goods to be returned to the plaintiff. After the sentencing, the defendant was released in court. Fei Shengxiang, Dan's lover, had also come to Shanghai after Dan was arrested and was in court yesterday to observe the proceedings. After Dan was released, she went back with Fei, leaving the courthouse.

Page 12

Da Chang Exchange Shop: A Bank Employee Steals from Himself. Theft of gold pounds, banknotes, and government bonds. After the crime, he and other people involved were arrested.

The Da Chang Exchange Shop, located at No. 2246 East-West Huade Road (now Changyang Road) in Hongkou, was jointly opened by Zheng Lianqing, Wang Xishu, and others. Zheng was the manager, and Wang was the assistant manager. Three years ago, they hired Xu Tixiang from Shaoxing, Yuyao as an apprentice. Xu is now 24 years old. Because he worked diligently, he was promoted to warehouse keeper this year, sharing the responsibility with Lou Dingfu. The warehouse of the Da Chang Exchange Shop was located in the kitchen. The key to the warehouse was usually kept by Wu Heting, the bookkeeper. At 8:30 PM on the 6th of this month, after the exchange shop closed, Xu Tixiang suddenly had a wicked thought.

Seeing that the warehouse key had not been locked, he secretly entered and stole American, Hong Kong, Canadian, and Singaporean gold pounds, banknotes, and national government bonds with a total face value of 10,961.50 yuan. He took the stolen goods and hid them elsewhere. The shop did not know about the theft at the time. It was not until 9:00 AM the next morning (the 7th) that they discovered the theft. However, they did not know who the thief was, so they did not report it to the police at the time. Until after 1:00 PM, Xu Tixiang suddenly claimed that his father, Xu Weihan, had come to Shanghai from his hometown a few days ago and was staying at the Jiangxin Hotel, No. 40 Jinli, Shanxi Road, in Room No. 1. He wanted to visit him. Manager Zheng Lianqing approved his request. Unexpectedly, Xu did not return. Manager Zheng then realized that the theft was related to Xu and urgently went to the Hongkou Police Station to report it. Detectives Huang Fusen, Bao Shuji, Bao Tan Ni Jialai, Zhang Chou Shan, Feng Qishan, and Western Detective Gedengbai were specially dispatched to Room No. 1 of the Jiangxin Hotel at 11:20 AM yesterday, where they successively arrested Xu Weihan and Xu Kang, Ye Maozhao, and Lou Yuliang (all from Yuyao), who were cooks on the Xianghe Steamboat. Under questioning at the police station, Lou Yuliang confessed that the stolen goods were hidden in his bedroom at the Fengtai Coal Shop, No. 366 Kangti Road (now Kangding Road) in the French Concession (Lou was the bookkeeper of Fengtai). He also stated that Xu Tixiang had boarded the Xianghe Steamboat, preparing to escape to Hankou. Chinese and Western detectives rushed to the Xianghe Steamboat at the Shuntai Wharf on Broadway Road (now Daming Road) to arrest Xu Tixiang. At the same time, they went to the Fengtai Coal Shop, searched and recovered all the stolen goods, and brought them back to the police station. At 3:30 PM, the police station sent Xu Tixiang and the other four to the 3rd Criminal Court of the First Special District Court. Zhang, a lawyer from the police station, presented the facts of the case, requesting a postponement. Zheng Lianqing and Wang Xishu, managers of the Da Chang Exchange Shop, also testified about the theft. When questioned, the defendant Xu Tixiang confessed to the theft, saying that because his salary was low and everything was expensive, his income could not cover his expenses, so he resorted to this strategy. However, he said that this was his personal act and that he had no connection with the other defendants. After stealing the gold pounds and other items, he asked his father, Xu Weihan, to keep them for him and his father then handed them over to Lou Yuliang and other fellow villagers. When Xu Weihan and the other four were questioned, their testimonies were evasive. Judge Xiao ordered the five defendants to be detained and the hearing postponed to Friday of this week. The stolen goods were returned first.

National Coal Industry Association: First Preparatory Meeting Convened. Division into bituminous and anthracite coal groups. Zhang Cuiping elected as the chief secretary of the preparatory committee.

The National Coal Industry Association's office convened its first preparatory meeting at its Foch Road (now Yan'an West Road) office at 10:00 AM yesterday (the 7th). Coal mine and factory representatives discussed various matters concerning the formal establishment of the association. The Ministry of Industry also specially dispatched Cheng Yifa, director of the Mining Affairs Department, from Beijing to Shanghai to participate. A reporter from the Dagong News Agency made a special investigation and reported the details as follows:

Participating Representatives

The coal mine representatives who participated yesterday included Wang Zimin of the Zhongxing Company, Liu Wanchun of the Changxing Company, Sun Mou of the Kailuan Mining Bureau, Zhang Hu of the Lieshan Company, Dai Linshu of the Huadong Company, Nie Huating of the Zhenglai Company, Xia Jiliang of the Jingxing Mining Bureau, Zhang Zijing of the Huainan Company, Zhang Shu of the Lu Da Company, Wang Jiliang of the Yuanhua Company, Sun Yueqi of the Zhongfu Company, Li Zucai of the Yili Company, Bai Yunxuan of the Baojin Company, Zhu Yonghe of the Datong Company, Zhang Zhongping of the Zhongxing Company, Li Guangqi of the Liuhegou Company, and Cheng Yifa, Director of the Mining Affairs Department of the Ministry of Industry, totaling over 30 people. Cheng Yifa served as the chairman.

Important Resolutions

After the customary ceremonies, the chairman reported on the significance of the previous coal mine meeting held by the Ministry of Industry, the process, and the resolutions passed. Subsequently, the following resolutions were passed: Regarding the matters of the preparatory committee, it was divided into two groups, bituminous coal and anthracite coal, to proceed. The bituminous coal group designated the Kailuan Mining Bureau, Datong Company, Pingxiang Liuhegou Company, Zhongxing, Huadong, Lu Da, Boshan Coal Mining Industry Association, Jingxing, Zhengfeng, Huainan, Datong, Changxing, and Bole companies to be responsible. The anthracite coal group designated Zhongfu, Pingding, Huxiang, Fuguo, Lihua, Yuanhua, Lieshan, Xieji, and Mentou companies to be responsible. Zhang Zhongping, chairman of the Mining Industry Association, was designated as the chief secretary of the preparatory office. For the drafting committee of the association's charter, the bituminous coal group designated Zhongxing, Yili, and Datong companies to be responsible for drafting. The anthracite coal group designated Zhongfu and Lieshan companies to be responsible for drafting. The drafted charter will be submitted to the association within two weeks for review. The next preparatory committee meeting was scheduled for July 5th. At the same time, the date for the second general meeting was also decided. Regarding the production, transportation, and sales methods of various coal mines, it was resolved to request the Ministry of Industry to consult with the Resources Commission to conduct an investigation to provide information for future reference. The meeting adjourned at approximately 2:00 PM.

Banquet for Representatives

It was also learned that Li Guangqi of Liuhegou, Zhu Yonghe of Datong, and Dai Linshu of Huadong, for the sake of fostering friendship, specially hosted a banquet at Yizhixiang and Dongya Restaurants yesterday to entertain the attending representatives and Cheng Yifa, Director of the Mining Affairs Department of the Ministry of Industry. Cheng Yifa, Director of the Mining Affairs Department of the Ministry of Industry, returned to Beijing by express train last night at 11:00 PM due to urgent official matters in Beijing.

Scolded by her Father, A Modern Female Student Commits Suicide

Yang Wenying, a young woman of 23 years old, lived at No. 7 Ci Hui Nan Li, Hartung Road (now Xikang Road) and was a student at a certain girls' middle school. Recently, Wenying was not diligent in her schoolwork and spent her time pursuing modern trends. Her father was very dissatisfied. Around 8:00 AM yesterday morning, her father severely scolded Wenying. Afterwards, Wenying secretly took poison in her room and committed suicide. She was discovered by her family, who immediately rushed her to the hospital for treatment. However, due to the severe poisoning, the treatment was ineffective. She died from the poison at 9:00 PM. The body was sent to the coroner's office to await an autopsy.

The Haiyuan Steamboat's Inspection is Complete; Resumption of Navigation Possible Within this Week

The new Haiyuan steamboat, the first completed ship built by the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company in England, was docked at the Jiangnan Shipbuilding Factory of the Navy some time ago for inspection of the hull and painting of the ship body, as it had been in service for two years. According to sources from the company, the inspection has now been completed, and the ship is expected to resume navigation within this week.

Huang Yousheng Commits Suicide by Poisoning

Huang Yousheng, a man from Guangdong province, 22 years old, was an apprentice at the Yonglixing Tea Shop at No. 422 Jiangxi Road. The day before yesterday (the 6th), Huang left without saying goodbye and opened Room No. 24 at the Hongkou Grand Hotel on North Sichuan Road. There was no movement overnight. At approximately 8:00 AM the next morning, a tea server on duty passed by the door of the room and heard moaning sounds inside. He quickly found a way to open the door and saw that Huang had ingested a large amount of potassium cyanide. There was poison residue around his mouth. Knowing that he had undoubtedly taken poison, he reported it to the Hongkou Police Station. An ambulance was dispatched to send him to the Tongren Hospital for treatment, but it was ineffective. He died at approximately 1:30 PM.

Xu Qingyun's Daughter Sues to Confirm the Invalidity of a Contract; Trial Concluded; Sentence to be Pronounced the Day After Tomorrow

Xu Qingyun, the deceased wealthy businessman and owner of Taichangxiang (three branches) and Qingchangxiang Foreign Goods Shop on Avenue Dubail (now Huaihai Middle Road), was from Pudong. He had assets of several million yuan. In his early years, he married a woman from his hometown, Chen, and had a daughter named Daxin (35 years old this year). Later, Xu took Chen as a concubine, and they had a son, Fusheng, and two daughters, Lanzhen and Huizhen. Afterwards, he abandoned his wife and daughter, ignoring them. His wife, Chen, sued Xu in the French court for favoring his concubine and neglecting his wife, along with a civil suit. A settlement was reached, and a divorce agreement was signed at the law office of Zheng Yuxiu, witnessed by lawyers Jin Yu, Ren Zhennan, and Li Xinyang, and drafted by Wang Jimen. Only Xu and Chen signed the agreement at the time. Xu Qingyun signed it two weeks later. Later, Xu's daughter Daxin discovered that her signature was on the divorce agreement, as well as a clause in the second article stating that the second party would never again claim the right to an analysis of the first party's assets. She objected to her father and filed a suit in the First Special District Court against the two lawyers, Zheng and Li, for breach of trust. The case was delayed until now due to the January 28th Incident. Recently, Xu Daxin hired three lawyers, Zhang Shizhao, Peng Yuanxun, and Zhang, and filed a suit in the Civil Court of the Second Special District Court against her father's concubine, Xu Chen, and her siblings, Xu Fusheng, Xu Lanzhen, and Xu Huizhen, seeking confirmation that the divorce contract signed by her deceased parents was invalid. Judge Ma Yishu has held several hearings, summoning witnesses Wang Jimen, Ren Zhennan, and Zhu Honglie for questioning. Due to the incomplete number of witnesses, he ordered a postponement. As reported in this newspaper, yesterday, another summons was issued for a continued hearing. The plaintiff Xu Daxin arrived with her lawyers. The defendants were still represented by lawyers. According to Xu Daxin's testimony, she was not present to sign at the time, and her signature was not a cross. The judge ordered Xu to write ten crosses and one name in court. Later, lawyer Jin Yu testified that Xu Chen and Xu Daxin, mother and daughter, were present to sign, and the clause stating that the second party could not claim an analysis of the first party's assets was added later. Lawyer Li Xinyang testified that Xu Chen received the written agreement several months later. Xu Daxin then wrote a letter questioning and objecting to the second clause. He did not know the content. At the time, he saw Chen sign two words, but he could not remember whether Daxin signed or not. He asked Daxin. At this point, the court understood the case and ordered the debate to begin. The plaintiff's lawyer stated that lawyer Jin Yu's testimony was biased towards Xu Qingyun, as he was a party involved. However, the testimonies of the other witnesses were consistent, indicating that Xu Daxin was not present to sign. He requested that the court rule the contract invalid. After the defendant's lawyer rebutted, the court declared the debate concluded and scheduled the verdict for 9:00 AM on the 11th.

Jingfeng Printing and Dyeing Company Sues Huang Shengchang for Embezzlement, Seeking Recovery of Over 3,000 Gold

Huang Shengchang, currently the factory director of the Weilun Woolen Mill at No. 12, Lane 21, Hubei Road, served as the general manager of the Jingfeng Printing and Dyeing Co., Ltd. at No. 1188, the intersection of Zhoujiazui Road and Dalianwan Road, from February 1, 1934, to July 31, 1935. He has since resigned. Recently, after Xie Meisan, the chairman of the company from Yuyao, commissioned Sun Zhongyao, an accountant, to audit the accounts, it was discovered that Huang had inflated accounts and embezzled public funds totaling 5,014.32 yuan in national currency during his tenure. They hired lawyer Dai Jien and filed a lawsuit against Huang Shengchang in the Criminal Court of the First Special District Court for embezzlement, requesting that he be punished according to Article 336, Paragraph 2 of the Criminal Code, as well as filing an ancillary civil lawsuit, requesting that he be ordered to return 3,014.32 yuan (because he had already returned 2,000 yuan). Yesterday afternoon, Judge Huang Risheng of the First Special District Court held a hearing in the 8th Criminal Court. The defendant Huang Shengchang arrived with his defense lawyer to respond to the lawsuit. After Xie Meisan stated the facts of the prosecution, the court questioned Huang Shengchang. As further investigation was required, he ordered a postponement of the hearing.

Robbery at a Cigarette Paper Shop on Chang'an Road; Passerby Shot

At approximately 1:00 AM yesterday morning, two robbers arrived at the Dafeng Cigarette Paper Shop at No. 424 Chang'an Road, under the jurisdiction of the Hengfeng Road Police Station in Zhabei. One robber was wearing a long blue cloth gown and a top hat, was tall, and had a dark complexion. The other robber was of medium height, had a square face, and a dark complexion. Each carried a 4-inch handgun. They pried open the back door and entered the room. At that time, everyone in the shop was asleep. The robbers immediately frightened them into silence, ransacked the boxes and chests, and stole 120 silver coins, 76,000 copper coins, one silk cheongsam, and over ten short shirts and trousers. After robbing, the robbers left the shop and attempted to escape. As they passed through the alley, Mao Shoufu, a man from Shaoxing who sold beef on Route Tenant de la Tour (now Tongfu Road) in the concession and lived at No. 21 in the alley, was returning home. Seeing one of the robbers looking flustered, Mao shouted "Catch the thief!", intending to arrest him. Unexpectedly, the robber fired several shots, one of which hit Mao's left arm, causing him to fall to the ground in pain. The robbers, realizing that they had caused trouble, fled. Yu Dongsen (52 years old, from Ningbo), the owner of the Dafeng Cigarette Paper Shop, and his neighbors heard the gunshots and went out to investigate, but the robbers were nowhere to be found. The victim prepared a list of the stolen items and rushed to report it to the Hengfeng Road Police Station. Chief Lu Peili, along with patrol officer Huang Zhenxiang and detectives Wu Zhongda, went to the scene to investigate. At the same time, they reported to the Inspectorate of the Public Security Bureau and ordered the detective squad to arrest the criminals and recover the stolen goods. Mao Shoufu, who had been shot, went to the Baolong Hospital on Rue Brenier de Montmorand (now Baike Road) in the concession for treatment. Fortunately, the injury was not critical and was not life-threatening.

Tailong Flour Company Holds Extraordinary General Meeting

The Tailong Flour Company was founded in the early years of the Republic of China and established a manufacturing factory in Wuxi. Its Eagle Ball and Dragon Boat brand flours are sold in major commercial ports at home and abroad and enjoy a good reputation. In 1931, it added new machines and increased capital for reorganization. However, it suffered heavy losses due to the impact of the Shanghai War. In January 1934, the shareholders' meeting resolved to instruct the board of directors to liquidate and end the company. However, due to the gradual decline in asset prices, the assets and liabilities were insufficient to offset each other, and it was even more difficult to find a suitable buyer due to the financial contraction. The liquidation process was difficult, so the factory had to be leased out to continue operations, using the rental income to pay off interest. It has been almost two years since then. On the morning of the 13th of last month, the factory's machine building, office, and other areas suddenly caught fire, and the machinery and equipment were completely destroyed. In addition to sending personnel to investigate and prepare a list of losses to claim compensation from the insurance company, the company held an extraordinary general meeting at its Shanghai office at No. 304 Tiantong Road at 3:00 PM on the 7th of this month. The key points of the decisions made are as follows: The shareholders elected Ye Shumei and Gu Yuxun as liquidators to handle all liquidation matters. The company will be dissolved after the liquidation is completed. In addition to sending the accounts to each shareholder for review, no further shareholders' meetings will be held.

Meeting of the Joint Council of the Second Special District

Second Special District Ninth Branch: 1. The Ninth Branch of the Joint Council of the Special District held its third membership meeting yesterday at the Mengjiangtang on Rue Crépel (now Ji'an Road) and re-elected the executive committee. Guo Shuliang, representative of the Second Special District General Council, and Zhang, representative of the Fourth Branch, delivered speeches. Subsequently, the proposals were discussed. The proposal that the Public Works Department should be asked to determine and implement the method of subsidizing Chinese education expenses in this special district was passed. The proposal that the French Water and Electricity Company was forcing new residents to pay the water and electricity bills owed by the previous residents and threatening to cut off water and electricity should be negotiated for rectification was passed. The proposal that the Public Works Department and French water and electricity companies often threatened to cut off water and electricity when citizens occasionally owed property tax or water and electricity bills, and then forced them to pay connection fees after the arrears were cleared should be negotiated for rectification was passed. The proposal on how to handle rental disputes in this district was passed, resolving to report to the Citizens' Association for mediation. The proposal that citizens should use domestic products was passed. The proposal on how to solicit members for the association was handed over to the executive committee for handling. The proposal on how to promote sanitation in this district was handed over to the executive committee for handling.

Weather Report

According to the meteorological forecast issued by the Xujiahui Observatory yesterday at 4:30 PM, a low-pressure area is developing in the East Sea, moving east or northeast-east. The weather around Shandong will change from sunny to cloudy, with southeast to southwest winds. The weather in the Hankou area will change from cloudy to overcast, with light and variable winds. The weather in the lower reaches of the Yangtze River will be overcast with light fog, gradually becoming cloudy, with northeast to northwest winds. There will be strong gales and heavy rain in the East Sea. The weather in the southern coastal areas and around Taiwan will be overcast with fog, and light southern winds. Furthermore, the highest temperature in Shanghai within the 24 hours before 3:00 PM yesterday was 66.0, and the lowest was 62.6. On the same day last year, the highest was 90.9, and the lowest was 64.4.

Letter to the Editor

To the Editor,

Regarding the news item published in your newspaper on the 6th of this month about the damage to our company's steamship at sea, which stated that the ship was leased to a Japanese company and traveled to various ports in Japan and Europe, the facts are not in accordance with the actual situation. Our company's steamship "Hai Shang Lun" was leased to the state-run China Merchants Steam Navigation Company to operate on the South China route. After the lease ended in June last year, it was taken back and operated by ourselves. It is currently sailing in India and has never been leased to the Japanese Datong Company, nor has it traveled to European ports. We are writing to you accordingly, hoping that your newspaper will investigate and correct the report to clarify the truth and value public opinion. Sincerely, China Merchants Steamship Co., Ltd. June 8th.

Chunqiu

Snippets

— (Xiao Bai)

Life is inherently a battle.

Learning has no end. We live in this world and must strive to enrich ourselves daily to meet the needs of our lives, understand this world, and develop the ability to cope with all kinds of emergencies.

People have two kinds of education: one is received from others, and the other is obtained through self-study. The latter is actually more important than the former.

We must learn, learn, and learn again, because the more we learn, the more we discover our own ignorance and mistakes, and correct and improve ourselves.

We cannot overestimate ourselves, but we must not underestimate ourselves either. We must know that one person has no power, but two people are a little stronger. When many people unite together, that can bring about a qualitative change and unleash extraordinary power.

In Memory of Mr. Yu Jianhua

— Qing

Alas, on the twentieth anniversary of the martyrdom of Mr. Chen Yingshi, Mr. Yu Jianhua, a pioneer of the Tongmenghui from my hometown of Taicang, passed away in Lidi. A genius of his generation was wasted by illness, unable to fulfill his ambitions to devote himself to the party and the group. He displayed extraordinary talent in writing, but ended his life in melancholy at the young age of fifty-two. His works include only the "Jianhua Collection," "The Legend of Pianhong," and "A Strange Book from the Wilderness," three titles in all. Mr. Yu had been ill for more than ten years, his children were young and weak, and his family was in poverty. Fortunately, he received assistance from Mr. Liu Yazi, Tao Xiaoliu, Ye Chucang, and Feng Xinxia, and his wife was virtuous and served him well, so that Mr. Yu was not troubled by trivial matters and his children did not miss a single day of school. Otherwise, the grass on Mr. Yu's grave would have been overgrown long ago. How could he have lived for another ten years and seen his children complete their studies? Mr. Yu's given name was E, his courtesy name was Jianhua, and his sobriquet was Yisu. He was a remarkable man from Loudong, skilled in poetry and unrestrained in drinking, and a talented member of the Nanshe. In his youth, Mr. Yu studied in Japan, working hard and striving for progress, and his studies were comparable to Meng Jin's. He later studied with Mr. Feng Xinxia at Aurora University, conspiring to destroy the stone statue of the Virgin Mary, which was disliked by the French. He then left and traveled around, to Shandong, Fujian, Guangdong, and Yan, and among the islands of Southeast Asia. Wherever he went, he associated with revolutionary patriots, and often contributed writings to revolutionary magazines. He also followed Mr. Chen Qubing, Liu Yazi, Gao Jiangong, and other gentlemen to the Nanshe, allying at the Zhang Gong Temple in Huqiu, Wuxian. Later, he taught poetry at Jinan University, but was frustrated and returned home due to illness, resting in seclusion in Yanshan, composing poems to express his feelings. He then commissioned a friend to paint a picture of "Dreaming and Chanting by a Small Window" to show his aspirations. However, in his youth, he traveled around with a staff, experiencing hardship and danger, and his spirit was heroic, like Fang Shanzhi discussing military affairs on horseback. Who knew that he would be debilitated by illness in less than twenty years! Initially, Mr. Yu suffered only from neurasthenia, then both hands twitched, and finally he suffered from total paralysis. However, his senses were not dulled. When guests visited him, his eyes would stare intently, and when asked a question, he would slowly utter one or two words after several minutes. His eating, living, and sleeping all depended on his wife. Alas, how bitter!

Rotten Pears

A Shen Bao Newspaper from Twenty-Eight Years Ago

— Choucheng

During the 30th anniversary celebration of joining the military held in Suzhou this time, all the comrades who attended sent various items used in the barracks thirty years ago to the meeting for display as a memento, and Huang Xinyi collected the most. In addition to the conscription handbook issued by the Changzhao Society in the thirty-second year of Guangxu, the congratulatory speech for welcoming new soldiers, and the salary sheet for the deputy squad leader of the left team of the first battalion of the second infantry regiment, and the exam papers for entering the army school, there was also a third sheet of this newspaper from the fifth day of the sixth month of the first year of Xuantong, because it was printed with a group photo of all the students of the 46th regiment's army school. At that time, this newspaper was still printed on one side with glossy paper. This photo was published on the second page of the third sheet, three inches high and five inches wide, very clear. Before the local news, there were eighteen characters above it: "Photography of the Fourth Semester of the Suzhou 46th Regiment Army School." The audience all regarded it as an antique and admired his meticulousness. At that time, the local news was divided into six columns: the inner city, the southern city, Zhabei, the British Concession, the American Concession, and the French Concession. There was a news item above: "Confiscating Morphine Syringes," which said, "Tian, the magistrate of this county, learned that in various villages in this county and at the borders of Fengxian, Qingpu, Huating, and Nanhui counties, some people were injecting morphine liquid syringes instead of opium. Ignorant people do not know the harm, only seeking temporary enjoyment, regardless of the poison entering their lungs and harming their lives in the future, which is very pitiful. Yesterday, he specifically ordered officials to go to the countryside and strictly arrest them to prevent future harm." Unexpectedly, after twenty-eight years, this kind of morphine syringe that harms people deeply has still not been completely banned, which is lamentable! There was also news about "Three Records of Fish Vendors' Strike," which said, "With the efforts of the directors of the Chamber of Commerce, it is hoped that it will be resolved. It is said that it will still follow the old rules and not change the foreign scale. As for the remaining follow-up measures, Yu Qiaqing, the observer, will issue a proper agreement within ten days and announce it again." It can be seen that Yu Qiaqing at that time was already mediating commercial disputes.

The Cruelty of Wearing Animal Skins

— Yimei

It is indeed a barbarian custom for people to wear animal skins. In ancient times, people did not know how to plant cotton and make clothes, so they hunted animals for their skins to keep warm. After Leizu invented silk and Huang Daopo created cotton, clothing was greatly improved, and there was no need for animal skins to decorate oneself. However, the habit was long-standing and not easily changed, and even now, fur coats are still highly valued. Yesterday, I heard Mr. Lu Shie say: "It is indeed a cruel act to cut and take animal skins, especially pearl skin grey rats. Pearl skin is not naturally like that. In the coldest days of winter, sheep are tied up and their hair is completely removed. Then they are pushed into the ice and snow. The sheep freeze to the extreme and tremble incessantly, and then fine hair grows into granular shapes, which is what is called pearl skin. Grey rats, also known as blue rats, are dark grey with white bellies and long, loose tail hair. They are agile and good at jumping. They are found in the mountains of Jilin. After they are caught, a red-hot iron skewer is inserted through the rat's anus. The rat is in great pain and struggles, and the oil seeps into the fur, giving it a luster when viewed. The sable is the most kind. Those who catch it take red arsenic in advance, lie naked in the snow. The sables know this and come to cuddle to keep warm. The naked person suddenly gets up and strangles them. Molten lead is forcibly poured into the sable's mouth. The sable is in extreme pain and rolls on the ground, and the oil also seeps out because of this." Therefore, although Mr. Lu wears fur coats, he absolutely does not wear pearl skin grey rat sable, he said.

A New Nest for Phoenixes

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter 2: A Beautiful Woman Leans on the Ripples of the Sky, a Good Dream Warmly Nurtured in the Moonlight of a Small Building

After he said this, he gave another knowing smile, took out the fountain pen he carried in his chest pocket, and densely wrote two lines of double circles next to the four words "lingering grievances of the remaining years." Then, he read the short story through, word by word. After reading it, he suddenly had some kind of feeling, and immediately searched through the bookshelves and cabinets, finding thirty or forty newly published magazines and placing them all on the table. The names of the magazines included "Spring Breeze," "Cuckoo's Voice," "Oriole's Song," and "Petals' Fragrance." The covers all featured extremely beautiful pictures. He randomly picked up a magazine and flipped through it wildly, looking for writings signed by "Yi Litian." He would look at the title and then, with the fountain pen, write the title in a very delicate English exercise book. After writing it down, he would flip through the second magazine. He searched through all the books, and then returned them to the bookshelves and cabinets. The English exercise book on the table, however, had quite a few words copied on it. He cleared the table, put the exercise book aside, and then took out a stack of red silk grid paper from the drawer, and used an ink brush to neatly transcribe the names of the novels from the exercise book again. Below each novel title, he wrote down which issue of the magazine it was published in, the total number of words, and what kind of content it was. He painstakingly copied for more than four sheets of paper. After he finished transcribing, he seemed pleased with himself, put down the pen, held the papers in his hands, and lay down next to a rattan chair to read, pondering the content of each novel. In his ears, he seemed to hear a slight rustling sound. When he looked up, it was the maid Xiao Ju, who had already entered the room. He asked, "Why are you being so sneaky? If you want to come in, just come in." Xiao Ju said with a smile, "I've come in two or three times. Miss was focused on copying books, and I didn't dare to disturb you." Menglan said with a smile, "You know that copying books shouldn't be disturbed." Xiao Ju said, "I don't know that. I see that Miss is putting all her energy into those books and papers. There must be some meaning to it." As she spoke, she couldn't help but smile. Menglan stood up, put the copied papers into a lecture folder, and said with a smile, "What are you smiling at?" Xiao Ju said, "The young mistress said that there are very interesting drum lyrics in these books. Miss, please tell me a few paragraphs one night." Menglan said, "Do you even know what drum lyrics are?" Xiao Ju said, "How could I not know? The young mistress also told me about 'The Jade Hairpin,' 'Three Smiles,' 'The Jade Dragonfly,' and 'Talented Scholars and Beautiful Ladies.' They're very interesting." Menglan said, "You even know about 'Talented Scholars and Beautiful Ladies.'" After saying this, she felt a great sense of emotion, so she rested her hands on her head and sat leaning against the back of the chair. When Xiao Ju saw her suddenly becoming sulky, she thought she had offended her with her words and left on her own. (32)

Special Feature

A Glimpse of the Fish Market

— Yafei

On a gloomy afternoon, I boarded the city ferry bound for the fish market.

The ferry left the double-layered pier amidst the noisy voices of the people, and the neon sign of the waterfront restaurant gradually disappeared before our eyes.

Sails fluttering, the river flowing leisurely; I stood on the deck, leaning on the railing, looking out at the outline of the metropolis, a dreamlike picture appearing before my eyes. The boat, gathering courage, moved forward, while many small boats and canoes cut through the surging waves, splitting the river surface, weaving back and forth like shuttles. The muffled whistles, like the braying of donkeys, made people's eardrums a little swollen. The gigantic imperial warships and merchant ships of Great Britain lay quietly in the heart of the river, revealing their hideous faces, like several man-eating demons!

An hour later, we had left the bustling center of the metropolis and passed through the factory area! Yangshupu; then, that milky yellow three-dimensional building vaguely appeared on the shore opposite Donggou Wharf. First, what we saw amidst the lush greenery was the national flag fluttering high in the sky; then came the eight large characters "Ministry of Industry Shanghai Fish Market."

I landed on the dock in front of me, where I met quite a few fashionable men and women who had come to visit.

Here, in addition to a very modern Western-style building, there was also a small vegetable market-style auction site. To the east was the fishing boat dock. At this time, more than a dozen fishing boats with bare masts were moored alongside the dock. Countless small iron rails were embedded horizontally and vertically on the dock and on the ground everywhere, for transporting fish away from the dock and to various places. There were three docks in total. The Western-style building housed the market office. The lower level had a small bank that specialized in lending capital to fishermen, named the Fisheries Trust Society Business Office. The fish market office had a total of five rooms, and other storage rooms, coolie rooms, telephone rooms, toilets, dining halls, etc. were all equipped. In addition to a general office on the second floor, there were also director's rooms, conference rooms, archive rooms, small offices, research rooms, libraries, technical rooms, supervisor's rooms, exhibition rooms, etc. The third floor was the staff dormitory and bathroom. The fourth floor was a terrace. The fifth and sixth floors had only one observation tower.

To the west of the auction site was the office of each broker—the fish shop—with a total of twenty-seven storefront rooms, each being the office of one broker. The business offices of the various fishing companies were on the second floor.

On the lower level were five large cold storage rooms, one ice-making room, two machine rooms, two manager's rooms, and several processing rooms; it is said that they could refrigerate a total of 1,500 tons of fish. The ice-making area was at the northernmost end.

The opening time for the auction was 3:30 AM, so when I went to visit, the market and office were quiet, only smelling a very unpleasant fishy odor.

Coming back, I went to Junpu Bureau Road for a week-long tour; there was a surveyor measuring on the side of the road, preparing to install small iron rails. There, the entire coast was a reed industry, and I saw many villagers picking reed chopsticks in the muddy reed fields, and there were quite a few men and women coming and going to the fish market.

Local Customs Anecdotes

Japanese Confectionery Passed Down from Our Country

— Jiyun

Confectionery is not fruit, but a kind of Japanese snack, similar to the mantou in our country. The inside is all purple bean paste, and the outside is wrapped in colored flour. It is red and green, very beautiful. Moreover, the style is not just round, there are all kinds. Japanese people call it "confectionery," but they still call our country's white mantou "mantou." But Japanese confectionery is also transformed from our country's mantou.

According to Japanese research, our country's mantou was invented in the Han Dynasty. "Origins of Things" records, "When Zhuge Liang conquered the south and was about to cross the Luzhu River, the local custom was to sacrifice to the gods with human heads. Liang ordered that sheep and pigs be used instead to take the dough human heads to sacrifice, and the name mantou began." At that time, China only had meat mantou, because it imitated the heads of barbarians, it was called barbarian head, and later it was transformed into mantou. "Seven Repair Drafts" records, "At first, it was written as barbarian head, starting from Zhuge Wuhou," which can prove it. Another saying is that mantou was originally called mantou, man meaning covered with dough, and tou being the first food in a banquet. Therefore, "Lu Chen's Sacrifice Method" has the sentence "spring shrine uses mantou." The two sayings do not say which is true, but it is undoubtedly created in the Han Dynasty.

The oldest mantou in Japan is the Shioze confectionery shop, which has a history of six hundred years. The first one to be introduced to Japan was Lin Jingyin from the Song Dynasty in our country. At that time, Zen Master Longshan of Kenninji Temple in Kyoto, Japan, entered the Song Dynasty, and Lin Jingyin returned to him as a disciple and went to Japan together, so there was Nara mantou. Lin Jingyin was a descendant of the hermit Lin Hejing. It is said that next to Lin Hejing's study, there was an anman tree. He imitated the shape of his fruit and made mantou, so the mantou of the Lin family at that time was famous.

Lin Jingyin married a wife in Japan and gave birth to two sons and two daughters. The eldest son, Mutou, became the founder of Ryosokuin in the Kenninji Temple Pagoda. The second son, Yuu Tenshu, changed to running a mantou business, opened in Kyoto's Karasuma Shijo Shimomachi, and was the founder of the Japanese confectionery shop. This place name is also commonly known as Mantouya-cho. Later, Yuu Tenshu's son, Shoban, went to our country to study for several years before returning to Japan and settling in Shioze Village. He changed his surname to Shioze, and Shioze mantou got its name from this.

During the Battle of Sekigahara in the Tokugawa era, Tokugawa Ieyasu used mantou placed in his helmet to worship heaven and earth and pray for victory. Therefore, there was also the name of Kabuto Mantou, and it became a food to reward the three armies. Japanese confectionery is completely used as a tea snack, so it has a close relationship with the tea ceremony. At that time, the noble class and the leisure class were very fond of the tea ceremony, so confectionery was valued along with it. Many elegant names were proposed, such as "Dancing Crane," "Hazy Night," and "Suhama," which are now famous confections.

Since the mantou business became popular, countless people imitated it. Although restrictions were agreed upon, there were still more than 200 shops in Kyoto City. Crude manufacturing and abuse were far from what they used to be. Tokyo was originally called Edo, and there was no such confectionery. It was not until Matsudaira Echizen-no-kami went to Saikyo and tasted the delicious mantou. So he specially went to Kyoto to summon a confectionery master to make it. Now there are confections everywhere in Japan. They are eating the mantou that was passed down from our country, or they still think it is a Japanese specialty.

In Chinese restaurants in Japan, because some of our Chinese students like to eat noodles, there are mantou and buns for sale. Not many Japanese are encouraged to eat it, because they always prefer sweet confections to meat mantou.

My Country's World Games Football Team: European Tour Miscellany, Written and Sent by Li Huitang

Arrival in Batavia

After our 4-0 victory over the Singapore Combined Team on September 14th, we set off the following afternoon on the Dutch mail ship "Plancius" towards Batavia, 500 nautical miles away. Teammate Cai Wenli, due to an important championship match involving the Singapore Chinese team, was delayed and only caught up with us three days later. The first half of this two-day, one-night voyage was quite comfortable, but later the weather changed, and the wind and waves became violent. At the final evening meal, less than half enjoyed it. Among them, Liang Rongzhao, Huang Meishun, Li Guowei, Chen Zhenhe, and others vomited incessantly. Most of the other friends were also depressed, huddling in their bunks. This sea route, which I have traveled more than ten times, had waves like I have not seen before. It could be said that the Dragon Palace was playing a prank. On the morning of the 17th, the Batavia harbor was already in sight. After the formalities of passport inspection by the immigration office, we disembarked in an orderly fashion. Welcoming us were the local community organizations, Deputy Consul Lin, and many people from the sports community. It was not lively, but it was not desolate either. After landing, we took cars into the city and checked into the Asia Hotel. At 11 o'clock, all the community organizations in Batavia held a welcome meeting at the Guang Zhao Public Hall, chaired by Consul General Song. The atmosphere was solemn. During the meeting, the chairman gave a welcoming speech, and Director Rong gave a speech of thanks. Then, a flag-presenting ceremony was held. The flag was inscribed with the eight characters: "Strive forward, win glory for the country." We accepted and were even more motivated. After the meeting, because of the oppressive heat and fatigue from the boat journey last night, we all stayed in our lodgings to rest, preparing to compete with the Batavia Combined Team, the champion of all the cities in Java, in the afternoon. (The match report will be recorded separately.) According to the schedule for the entire island of Java, we will stay for three weeks and play more than ten matches in various places. The schedule is tight, and from now on, the front line will become a time of many events. Batavia is the capital of the Dutch East Indies, where the governor resides. Commerce is thriving, making it a hub for transportation. Most of the Chinese are from Fujian and Guangdong, holding the reins of commerce. Many people say that if all the Chinese were to move out of the Dutch East Indies, the prosperity of the Dutch East Indies would plummet. This shows the position of our compatriots here. Four years ago, I lived here with my wife and children for eighteen months. I heard and saw a lot about the various local people. I know them quite well. The Dutch government's tax rate here is extremely harsh, but the politics are outstanding, and the city is peaceful. It is not like many places in our country, where taxes are heavy, and there are no achievements, leaving the people in deep water. The biggest exports of the entire island are sugar and coffee. The highways extend in all directions, making transportation convenient, which is unparalleled in the East. Except for Guowei and Jia Youliang, all of our team members have been here many times. Since 1929, the football teams from Hong Kong and Shanghai have come almost every year, leading the football craze on the island. Its popularity is far greater than in our country, and its spirit of progress is also very exemplary. Every year, they invite strong teams from Europe or East Asia to visit, in order to increase the benefits of mutual learning. Therefore, their technical progress has been rapid in recent years. Compared with our country's standing still, there is simply no comparison.

Narrow Victory Over the Batavian Selection

Last night, many felt uncomfortable due to the waves during the voyage. This morning (May 17th), we just landed on the mainland, rested for a few hours, and then competed with the Batavian Selection team, the champion of all the cities on the island, at 5 pm. We were cautious and nervous, fearing failure. At 4:30 pm, we arrived at the Kamit Budo Stadium, only to see a sea of people. The entire stadium was already in disarray due to the large number of people. After taking photos according to custom, we lined up and waited. Our team lineup is on the left. The result was a 2-1 victory, with Feng Jingxiang and Li Huitang each scoring one goal.

Ten-Event Athletics Test: Zhang Lingjia Wins Championship with Total Score of 5154

In the ten-event athletics test for the World Games preliminary selection, the participants were Zhang Lingjia, Zhou Changxing, and Cheng Mengping. Zhou Changxing had an advantage in the first half. The second half continued yesterday afternoon in the rain. The three competed extremely hard, but Zhou suffered a great loss in the discus throw. The javelin was his specialty, but because the field was too wet, it was difficult to display his strengths, resulting in a difficult situation to recover from. Cheng Mengping also lost a lot of points because he did not fully exert himself in the discus and 1500-meter events. Zhang Lingjia relied on good luck in the high jump and discus events to turn defeat into victory, scoring 5154 points to win first place. Second place went to Zhou Changxing, and third place to Cheng Mengping. The full results are listed on the left.

Education News

City Scout Convention: Camping Cancelled Yesterday Due to Rain; Troops Return Home, Curriculum Competition Rescheduled

Yesterday was the third day of the 7th City Boy Scout Convention. The memorial week was scheduled for the morning, and the curriculum competition was scheduled for the afternoon. However, the weather did not cooperate. The wind and rain started the night before, and the campsite became a swamp, with mud everywhere, making it impossible to move. The boy scouts' clothes and shoes were soaked, and they were in a very embarrassing state. Therefore, Leng Xueqiao, the director of the convention affairs, convened a meeting of all troop leaders at the main office yesterday morning and decided that due to the weather conditions, camping had to be cancelled. The curriculum competition will be announced and rescheduled to be held at the City No. 1 Sports Field on Daji Road in the Nanshi area. Thus, the once grand convention came to a temporary end. The boy scout troops from various groups braved the rain to break camp, and the motor companies made three times their usual profit. Last night, the City Chamber of Commerce, Huacheng, Postal Workers, and Wusong Middle School troops stayed at the campsite. It was especially commendable that the City Chamber of Commerce and Wusong Middle School troops continued camping as a whole. The general office of the convention will continue to work at the campsite today, and will move back to the Nanshi Boy Scout Council office tomorrow. A reporter from the Guomin News Agency made a special trip to inspect the campsite last week. The following is a brief account of the campsite's behind-the-scenes stories.

Uninvited Guests Greatly Disappointed

On the night of the 7th, two masters of the wind graciously visited the venue as uninvited guests, causing all the boy scouts to frown. On the morning of the 8th, the masters were still reluctant to leave. The troop leaders were like ants on a hot pot, and held an emergency meeting. Of the thirty-six stratagems, breaking camp was the best policy. Otherwise, the children would catch a cold, and how would they take care of the aftermath? Therefore, it was decided to cancel camping and reschedule the competition. Everyone broke camp, greatly disappointed.

Non-stop Telephone and Constant Cars

With the decision to cancel camping, the troops prepared to leave. Therefore, the telephone specially installed for the convention was surrounded by people making calls. You called for moving trucks, and I called for passenger cars. From 5 o'clock to noon, the telephone did not stop. At the same time, in front of the city government, cars came and went constantly, never stopping. They came empty and left fully loaded.

Burning Down Camps in the Misty Rain

The boy scouts braved the rain to break camp, covered in mud. The cars were also slow in coming, and they were impatient while waiting. They sought pleasure in suffering, burning fires for fun. Therefore, the straw that they had slept on last night was subjected to a major fire robbery. For a while, the entire venue was ablaze, and the misty rain filled the sky, like a miniature of the burning of seven hundred miles of camps. It was also a special program of the convention.

Remaining Courage and Finding Happiness

The Shanghai Provincial No. 1 Middle School band is the only good military band in the city's boy scout community. It also played music during the grand review, and its melodious tunes were praised by the audience. Yesterday afternoon, almost all the troops had left, but they still held their old camp, blowing and broadcasting, crying and beating. It can be said to be the "finale" of the convention, not afraid of the wind and rain, drumming up their remaining energy, and finding their own fun in the tents.

Remaining Straw: A Scramble

The number of straw remaining at the campsite was still not small. The nearby poor people were very envious when they saw it. At first, they asked the boy scouts for it, but later they moved it in large numbers. The soaked, leftover straw was like a treasure. They grabbed it from each other, tied it up, and carried it away. It was an unexpected harvest, and the poor people benefited a little.

Actively Promoting the Bald Head Movement

Chairman Chiang advocated the New Life Movement, and the people in various places implemented the New Life Movement. The Zhenshi and Dagong schools in this city took the lead in the bald head movement. Those who heard the news and followed suit were still a small number. During this convention, Xie Yanbo and Yu Julu, the deputy general directors of the campsite inspection and command, believed that the bald head was indeed economical and hygienic, and could also show a spirit of courage. Therefore, they shaved their heads in public at the campsite. A certain boy scout from the Youth Association Middle School wielded the knife, so it did not cost a penny, which was extremely economical. It is a pity that no one followed them, letting the two of them enjoy the beauty alone.

Copper Mountain Teachers Strike Due to Eight Months of Unpaid Salaries

(Xuzhou, August 8th Dispatch) Copper Mountain teachers have been owed salaries for eight months. The Teachers' Association demanded salaries from the county government, but it has not been resolved. Starting from the 8th, all county-run schools will go on strike.

Executive Yuan Issues Order: Encourage and Guide People to Assist in Free Education

In order to encourage and guide local people to assist in the promotion of free education, the Ministry of Finance requested the Executive Yuan to order the finance and education departments of each province to approve when examining proposals: 1. Any local people who, after public discussion, are willing to share the expenses of free education; 2. Any local educational institutions that stipulate within each elementary school district that the expenses of free education be solicited or shared from each household according to its wealth. The Ministry of Education should also give appropriate awards depending on the circumstances. The Executive Yuan issued an order to the provincial governments on the 8th to forward the order for compliance.

Gao Nushi Scholarship to Continue Soliciting Articles Next Year

Hua Guozhen of Zhejiang University was selected for the China Science Society's Gao Nushi Memorial Scholarship essay this year. The scholarship for the 24th year has been announced. The 25th year has also begun to solicit articles, limited to the subject of biology. The details are as follows:

The announcement of the solicitation of articles for the 24th year. The solicitation of articles for the Gao Nushi Memorial Scholarship for the 24th year is limited to the subject of chemistry. There were dozens of applicants from more than ten schools, including Zhejiang University, Guangxi University, Zhijiang University, Datong University, Soochow University, Jinan University, and Hujiang University. After evaluation by the essay selection committee Zeng Zhaolun, Zhuang Changgong, etc., Hua Guozhen, a student in the Department of Chemistry at National Zhejiang University, was selected. The title of the essay is Heavy Hydrogen and Heavy Water. The first prize is a gold medal and a prize of 100 yuan, which has been remitted to the authorities of Zhejiang University to be forwarded to Hua.

The solicitation of articles for the 25th year continues. The solicitation of articles for the 25th year has continued, limited to the subject of biology. Anyone who is currently studying pure science in domestic universities and colleges can participate. The word count is stipulated to be more than 5,000 words and less than 10,000 words. The deadline is from now until November 31st. After the manuscripts are collected, experts will be hired to evaluate them, and the results will be officially announced in mid-February next year.

Commercial News

Finance: Foreign Telegrams Indicate Bullion Prices Recovered After Falling, Closing at the Same Price as Saturday

The gold market initially showed strength yesterday with the rise of raw gold, but later gradually declined due to strong selling pressure from banks and loosening of the domestic market. Major players seized the opportunity to buy aggressively at lower prices, and the market finally rebounded. In the early morning, the overseas silver market saw gains in London while remaining steady in the US. Forward prices in Montreaux rose by 1.3 to 1.8 percentage points. Exchange rates rose slightly. London spot gold rose by 2.5 pence. The Central Bank's listed prices were announced, with both the British pound and US dollar remaining unchanged. The Customs gold unit rose by 4 percentage points. The standard bullion price was listed at 1118.3 yuan, an increase of 1.5 yuan. Tong Taichang and others took advantage of the high price to sell bars, dropping the price to within 1 yuan. The market remained stable after opening, but with multiple parties selling off and banks actively unloading, prices gradually fell below 40 yuan. The Hong Kong and Shanghai Banking Corporation (HSBC) announced its listed prices, with both the British pound and US dollar remaining unchanged. At this point, the market hovered around 40 yuan, but selling pressure remained active. The silver equalization tax was announced, rising by half a percentage point, but still declined. Although major players took advantage of low prices to replenish their holdings, pushing the price back above 40 yuan at one point, those seeking to sell at high prices were still eager. At noon, the overall trend was flat and weak. The afternoon market opened steadily, with stronger buying interest from major players. Adding to this, Reuters reported positive buying news, gradually pushing the price above 40 yuan. Indian silver was reported to have increased by one anna, and the market hovered around 40 yuan. As major players' buying interest intensified, the market finally rebounded. Below is a record of the day's market conditions:

The morning opening was 1140.9 yuan, an increase of 0.6 yuan from last Saturday. Chun Yuan Yong Shang advanced to 1.3 yuan. Hui Xiang Yuan Mao Yong Ding Kang Heng Yu Yuan Yi Fu Da sold off, retreating to 39.6 yuan. Chun Yuan Yong Ding Kang took advantage of the low price to advance to 40.4 yuan. Da De Cheng sold off. HSBC's annual interest rate was announced, with both the British pound and US dollar remaining unchanged, and the market hovered around 40 yuan. Da De Cheng, Tong Taichang, Qing Fa, Yong Da Fa, and Yong Yuan Chang Yong all sold off. Although the silver equalization tax rose by half a percentage point, it still fell to 38.8 yuan. Da De Cheng, Da Lai, Chun Yuan Yong, and Qing Fa Yong maintained their positions at low prices, rising together to 40.1 yuan. Da De Cheng, Ding Kang, Fu Xing Yong, and Yi Cheng, among others, supplied at high prices, gradually dropping the price to 38.7 yuan. After some fluctuation, the noon closing was 1138.8 yuan, with a flat and weak market after the closing.

The afternoon market opened at 1138.9 yuan. Heng Yu Yuan Mao Yong Fu Xing Yong and Hui Xiang actively purchased bars, rising from 8.8 yuan to 9.9 yuan. Chun Yuan Yong and Tong Taichang took advantage of the high price to supply, dropping the price to 9.5 yuan. Reuters telegraphed news from Guangdong. Da De Cheng, Qing Fa Yong Da, and Heng advanced to 40.3 yuan. Fu Xing Yong and Heng Chang Yong sold off, retreating to 0.2 yuan. Heng Yu purchased bars, stabilizing the overall trend. The closing was 1140.3 yuan. After the closing, Da De Cheng and Hui Xiang, among others, made slight purchases, bringing the price to above 41 yuan.

The settlement price, based on the Central Bank's standard bullion listing, rose to 1128.3 yuan, an increase of 12 yuan based on the closing price, and a decrease of just over 1 yuan compared to last Saturday. This month's account balance is 1135 yuan, and July's is 1139 yuan. The morning water replenishment was 1135 yuan, and the afternoon was 1136 yuan. The pure gold price, adding 5 yuan, was 1145.9 yuan. Spot market conditions and swaps were quiet. Tianjin goods, adding 11 yuan, were used for smelting red gold.

Trading within the market was relatively flat. Overall, Chun Yuan Yong, Qing Fa Yong, Ding Kang, Yuan Chang Yong, Da Heng, Sheng Yuan Yong, Yi Cheng, and Da De Cheng Yuan Mao Yong were on the buying side, while Fu Xing Yong, Qia Feng Yong, Hui Xiang Shen, Da Yong Heng Chang Yong, Tong Tai Lu, and Shun Li were on the selling side. Fu Yu advanced first and then exited, while Hong Kang Yong and Heng Yu exited first and then advanced.

The day's market conditions were unstable. The morning opening was 1140.9 yuan, and the later closing was 1140.3 yuan. The highest price was 1141.3 yuan, and the lowest price was 1138.7 yuan, a fluctuation of 2.6 yuan. The result was the same price as last Saturday. This month, after deducting public orders, there are 336 bars remaining, with 7 long positions and 2 short positions. July futures have 12,313 bars, with 46 long positions and 36 short positions. The total volume traded was 6,524 bars in the morning and 3,283 bars in the afternoon.

Yesterday, Da De Cheng closed out 14 public order short positions. Today, Yi Cheng should take them in. The settlement price is 1135 yuan.

Securities: Government Bond Prices Fluctuating

Yesterday, due to the Chinese Securities Exchange's repeated debunking of rumors, public sentiment was relatively stable, leading to short covering by retail investors and a surge in prices. However, concerns arose due to the early three-week vacation for the education sector in Guangdong Province. Western newspapers continued to spread rumors, leading to a weakening trend. Major players continued to sell in the market, and the inventory of the Northwest Disaster Relief Association continued to flow out, absorbing cash and buying foreign exchange, leading to a continuous outflow of cash. Coupled with the serious problem of smuggling, the bond market itself was deeply affected, and the future remains uncertain. Yesterday's developments: at the morning opening, retail investors bought, and the No. 6 bond also saw short covering, rising by 2 to 4 jiao. In the second session, prices continued to rise, with the No. 35 bond and others seeing demand, rising another 1 to 3 jiao, a small rebound, which was also expected. In the afternoon, the situation weakened again. Selling of the No. 4, 16, and 34 bonds caused a small decline of 1 to 2 jiao. At the closing, unfounded rumors spread again, and selling of the No. 4, 16, and 22 bonds surged, leading to a slightly sharper decline, falling another 0.5 to 4.5 jiao. Overall, most market prices were still slightly better by about 1 jiao. The total volume traded was 5.52 million yuan. Yarn and Cotton: Spot Sales Improve, Cotton Yarn Decline Slows Slightly

The yarn market was calm, with the overall trend remaining in a state of fluctuation and hovering. However, spot yarn sales and demand from Sichuan and Yunnan continued to be strong, boosting sentiment. However, in general, speculative traders, aware that the negative sentiment has not yet dissipated, are inclined to sell. Furthermore, rumors circulated that Dafu may deliver goods on behalf of a certain party this month, further weakening the market.

Delivery Expected for Yarn This Month

The opening of the front market for standard yarn was weak due to the fatigue of foreign cotton and poor market sentiment. There were also rumors that the large quantity of yarn purchased last month by Dafu may be delivered this month, causing the monthly trend to be sluggish, the sentiment of the people to be lazy, and the market price to go downstream slowly. As a result, the prices for each month were lower by 2, 3, and 4 jiao respectively than the closing price of the previous day, but the price for November rose by only 1 jiao. At the opening of the afternoon market, the downturn in recent months became more intense, because rumors could not be dispelled, but people later heard that Sichuan and Yunnan traders had purchased more than 2,000 bales of spot yarn, boosting confidence and slightly increasing market prices.
