Shen Bao Medical and Pharmaceutical Supplement

Two Red Peaches (Part 2)

— Fan Shou

During my illness these past few days, what disappointed me most were the daily "antipyretic injections." Normally, I have a considerable faith in these kinds of antipyretic injections. When I encountered friends and relatives with minor fevers, using them always had nine effective results out of ten, remarkably effective. But when I used them on myself, the magic weapon failed. During the three days of high fever, each day after the injection, my body temperature actually increased by one and a half degrees. I can only say that the antipyretic injections were not lucky on my body. Of course! It is definitely not the case that antipyretic injections would increase body temperature. Undoubtedly, it was because the time of the injection was precisely when my "fever" was most severe.

Conversely, there were also things that satisfied me during these few days of illness. The thing that satisfied me most was an ice pack. On the second night of high fever, because I could think of no other way, I finally thought of using an ice pack. Sure enough! It must have been the time for the ice pack to have good luck. After using it, it immediately made me feel less faint and painful, and my mind was clear. Even more remarkably, after applying it for an hour, the fever actually dropped by about two degrees. Placing an ice pack on the head of a patient with a high fever can make the mind clearer; this is a natural principle and can be said to be understandable. But to say that it can reduce fever may not be consistent with the facts, right? After I used it, the fever dropped. This may have been a coincidence: the time of using the ice pack happened to coincide with the time when the body temperature was dropping. So, although the decrease in body temperature after using the ice pack is a fact, it cannot be denied that it was a coincidence.

However, applying an "ice pack" during periods of high fever is indeed a very reasonable and "kingly way" to reduce fever. Our people can greatly adopt it and should not be doubted by the mystical sayings of old doctors.

Originally, tonsillitis is not considered a particularly serious disease; it is mostly a symptom of many diseases. However, when it happened to me, it lasted a full week, with high fever for three or four days. Among tonsillitis cases, it can be considered a severe one. Why is it more severe when it happens to me? This may have something to do with my usual constitution, being healthy and rarely sick. In general, healthy and strong people are rarely sick on weekdays, so when they get sick, it is often more severe than others. This is indeed the case: for example, with typhoid fever, if the patient is healthy and strong, it is often more severe than in ordinary people. What's the reason? Is it because healthy people are usually less likely to be infected by minor pathogens, and when they do get sick due to infection, it proves that the pathogenicity of the few pathogens is particularly fierce and powerful? — We can only observe it as such.

Now, the tonsillitis is completely cured, and the "red peaches" have disappeared without a trace. If you ask: What medicine cured it? I can't answer. If I were to answer, I would have to say: My own body cured it. So the main credit for this recovery should still go to my own body. For example, during the high fever, injections and medicines were not effective. At least it can be said that the effect was not obvious. Later, after a certain period, the fever went away on its own. Isn't this self-healing function a function of the body itself? From then until the complete recovery, it was all like this: it didn't rely on any medicine, but on the troops mobilized within my own body! (Whole-body reaction) The merit of fighting the enemy hard! If we were to talk about the function of medicine, then, for ailments like my tonsillitis this time, at most it can only occupy the position of a few quartermaster soldiers in the army.

However, in some special diseases, the function of medicine is still very significant. It is indispensable. Its effectiveness is no less than Guan Yu's Azure Dragon Crescent Blade or Zhang Fei's eighteen-foot spear! Therefore, treating all medicines as insignificant logistics soldiers is also a wrong view!

So, how did I treat this bout of tonsillitis with medication?

My use of medication was very simple. When I started to have a slight fever and my throat was slightly red, I treated it as a cold with some throat inflammation. I prescribed 25cc of castor oil to clear my bowels, used some mouthwash for my throat, and also used a mild antipyretic. The next day, seeing that the condition had not improved but had worsened, I decided to abandon all medicines and conduct an investigation. The most important test was a blood test. So I took my blood to be tested to see if there were any pathological changes. At this time, I asked Dr. Sha here to take charge of the diagnosis. His idea was also to wait for the blood test report before making a decision. At present, we can only wait and do not need to use any medicine, nor should we use medicine indiscriminately. On this day, in addition to local throat antiseptic tablets and antiseptic mouthwash, I had an antipyretic injection at night due to the high fever. (This type of antipyretic injection can be used safely for various infectious fevers; it can be said that this type of "universal fever-reducing injection" is still the right medicine for ailments like tonsillitis.) But in the end, I was very disappointed! When I got the injection, it was 39 degrees, and an hour later, the fever had not subsided but continued to rise, reaching 40 degrees. Didn't this antipyretic injection of mine fail to "reduce fever" at all? — No, if I hadn't gotten this injection, my fever might have risen even higher, perhaps reaching 41 degrees! When medicine enters the body and does not show immediate results, we can only interpret it as follows:

The blood test report came! No malaria parasites, white blood cell count of 6,200, and very little left shift of white blood cells. With this, we can know: It is definitely not malaria. Second, suspected typhoid fever is also very unlikely because the white blood cell count in typhoid fever is usually much lower. (The number of white blood cells in ordinary infectious fevers always increases, but only typhoid fever decreases compared to ordinary people, which is an important characteristic!) At the same time, if it is typhoid fever, the left shift of white blood cells will also increase significantly. So, according to the blood test results, typhoid fever is very unlikely. At that time, I was greatly relieved about the suspected illness (typhoid fever) that I had been worried about in advance.

During the following two days of high fever, the medication used was roughly the same; or rather, no special medicines were used at all. Locally, needless to say, I still used some throat disinfectant. "Antipyretic injections" were given as usual, one injection per day because this is something that is guaranteed to be harmless. Even if the "benefit" is not obvious, the harm is always absolutely guaranteed to be absent. The oral antipyretic was not used at all during the days of high fever, except for a little on the last day. Why did I always avoid using antipyretics to reduce my high fever? The reason is still fear of typhoid fever! Although the blood test report clearly stated that it was not like typhoid fever, my body temperature only differed by one or two degrees, and it did not completely subside. Especially when I had a high fever of 39 or 40 degrees, my pulse did not increase in parallel with my body temperature, and it remained between 80 and 90 beats per minute. This made me unable to completely ignore the one or two points of suspicion that it was still typhoid fever. (This is also a characteristic of typhoid fever! The patient's pulse does not increase in parallel with body temperature. In ordinary fever patients, when the body temperature reaches 39 or 40 degrees, the pulse per minute is always above 100, even as high as 120 or 130 beats; but typhoid fever patients are different: even if their body temperature rises to 40 degrees, the pulse per minute mostly remains between 80 and 90 beats. — Of course, there may be exceptional cases.)

It is not advisable to use antipyretics frequently in patients with typhoid fever. Some people probably do not understand this reason. Here, I will explain it briefly. Everyone knows that typhoid fever has a certain course of time. The fever period of an ordinary typhoid fever is four weeks. This, of course, refers to a purely simple typhoid fever. If other ailments are mixed in, resulting in so-called "complications," then the time will have to be extended. Just the time for a simple typhoid fever is already quite long. During these four weeks, the typhoid bacteria are wreaking havoc in the human body for four weeks, causing inflammation for four weeks. During this time of inflammation and havoc, the human body will naturally produce a defensive and resistant phenomenon. This phenomenon is increased body temperature, which is "fever." When a country is attacked by an enemy, it cannot avoid mobilizing troops to resist the foreign enemy. When the human body is attacked by pathogens, the inside of the human body must also mobilize troops to show resistance and kill the enemy. The so-called increase in body temperature is a representation of the human body mobilizing troops to resist and fight when it is attacked by pathogens. In typhoid patients, the consumption of the whole body's nutrition under this several weeks of mobilization of troops and high fever reaction is very considerable; at the same time, the work of the heart is also exceptionally hard. The positive effect of antipyretics is temporary fever reduction, but its side effect is harming the heart! If antipyretics are used for the high fever of typhoid patients, the effect is very weak. After use, it may drop slightly temporarily, but because of the disease itself, it will soon return and rise again, which is of no help. However, the patient's heart has already suffered great harm. If used too much, on the one hand, the heart is already very tired and overworked due to the long-term fever, and on the other hand, it is stimulated by everything, making the heart weaker. Eventually, there will be a time when it cannot bear the burden, and at this time, it can only announce a strike and move toward a state of collapse. The reason why antipyretics should not be used for typhoid patients is that they do not have the benefit of reducing fever but have the harm of hurting the heart. The reason why I never used antipyretics during the days of high fever was also to be careful, so as to avoid being harmed "in case" something happened. (End)

Precautions and Prevention During Eye Disease Season

— Translated by Zi Fu

Late spring and early summer are the season for eye diseases. Dust in the city and pollen in the countryside ride the strong winds of early summer, floating in all directions, eager to find a place to rest on people's clothes, hair, or skin. As a result, the chances of eyes being harmed are particularly high. Every year during this period, there are more eye disease patients, which is indeed good evidence.

Wind is indeed a major enemy of the eyes. Due to the stimulation of strong winds, it is very easy to cause minor problems such as eye congestion or tearing. This is not a major concern. However, the arrival of wind is inevitably accompanied by dust. Once it enters the eyes, it is very easy to cause illness. Therefore, during this season, people who already have chronic eye diseases are prone to worsening of their conditions, and people with healthy eyes are also prone to various eye diseases during this period. Therefore, people who already have conjunctivitis or other eye diseases should pay special attention and it is best to go to a doctor for examination and thorough treatment from time to time. However, prevention beforehand is better than treatment afterwards. Therefore, the best approach for people with healthy eyes is to pay attention to prevention in order to safely pass through this eye disease season.

Eye diseases caused by strong winds mixed with large amounts of dust are primarily conjunctivitis. Indeed, sometimes you get lucky and only get simple conjunctivitis from this kind of stimulation, which is considered good luck. If bacteria are mixed in with the dust and enter the eyes, it is very easy to develop acute conjunctivitis (epidemic eye disease), with more severe eye diseases such as eye congestion, tearing, and swelling. Especially in the countryside, if pollen flies into the eyes, it will immediately cause conjunctivitis.

Another point is that whenever wind blows dust into the eyes, tears will come out. At the same time, people who lack hygiene knowledge will naturally use their hands to wipe their eyes. As a result, the bacteria attached to the dirty fingers will be transmitted into the eyes, which can easily cause epidemic eye diseases or styes. The so-called stye,

Page 16

also known as a "pig sty" or "eyelash sore," is caused by bacteria entering the hair root of the eyelash and causing suppuration.

So, how can we defend ourselves against the harm of wind and dust? A relatively easy way is for people who don't usually wear glasses to wear glasses during this time. Of course, just wearing glasses is not enough. It is best to wash your eyes carefully with clean, cold water when you return from going out. The method is to use cotton or a clean towel dipped in cold water in a washbasin to gently wipe the eyes separately. Doing this can have two effects: first, it washes away the impurities attached to the eyes and surroundings. Second, it is also a good cold compress that lowers the temperature of the eyes to eliminate eye congestion caused by wind and dust irritation.

In addition, it is important to pay close attention to washing your hands before washing your eyes, so as not to rub your eyes with dirty hands. Also, when traveling on the street and encountering dust flying into your eyes, do not panic and rub your eyes indiscriminately. When dust enters the eyes, it will naturally stimulate the production of a large amount of tears, which is a natural way. Because once tears flow out, they will naturally wash away and remove the dust. If we rub it indiscriminately, the dust will be forced to pierce in all directions and penetrate deeper, which is truly asking for trouble. If the dust is not easy to remove, you should go to a doctor for examination when necessary.

Also, when tears flow out with dust, use a clean handkerchief to gently wipe it away. Avoid rubbing your eyes with unclean hands, because this is not only useless but also has many harms.

Domestic Medicinal Plants (Continued)

— Zhou Mengbai

Rubia cordifolia, L. var. Mungista, Mig.

(Plant) Grows wild in the mountains and fields. It is a perennial creeping plant. The roots are yellowish-red, hence the name "Rubia." The stem is square and has barbs. The leaves are in whorls of four, with long petioles and pointed oval shapes, with three to six main ribs. Conical cymes emerge from the leaf axils, and white five-petaled flowers bloom in autumn. The berries are spherical and turn black when ripe.

(Ingredients) Among the components of this plant, the only one that has been definitively proven is Purpurin C6H4＜　＞C6H(OH)3 (1.2.4).

(Medicinal Uses) It is said that Rubia roots can be used as a medicine to promote menstruation for women. They can also be used as a hemostatic for hemoptysis (coughing up blood), epistaxis (nosebleeds), and hematuria (blood in urine). They also have antipyretic and tonic effects. The dosage is 8 grams, decocted.

(Other Uses) The roots can be used as a dye, but this is rarely done today.

Common Sense Questions and Answers About Diseases

— Cheng Hanzhang

(83) Acute Generalized Miliary Tuberculosis

(Tuberculosis miliaris acuta)

Q: What is acute generalized miliary tuberculosis?

A: This is a disease in which a person who already has tuberculosis suddenly develops miliary tuberculous nodules all over the skin with chills and high fever. It is caused by tuberculous bacteria entering the bloodstream.

Q: Why does tuberculosis suddenly develop into this kind of disease?

A: It is mostly because the body suddenly encounters a weakening trigger. Such as suffering from acute infectious diseases, pregnancy and puerperium, mental and physical overwork, bone and joint and gland tuberculosis, etc.

Q: What are the symptoms of acute generalized miliary tuberculosis?

A: It usually starts with chills and high fever, sometimes accompanied by headache, vomiting, or other gastrointestinal symptoms. The fever type is often continuous or remittent. Chills and shivering recur repeatedly during the course. The pulse is rapid, and the blood pressure decreases.

Q: What are the respiratory symptoms in people with this disease?

A: Respiratory symptoms include cough (dry cough), sputum, shortness of breath, cyanosis. The lung area is tympanitic and dull on percussion, emphysema; in the late stage, there is no breathing sound.

Q: Are there any neurological symptoms?

A: The neurological disorders initially complain of severe headache, tinnitus, and dizziness, and later become unstable, delirious, and drowsy. Eventually, symptoms resembling meningitis appear (that is, neck stiffness, Kernig's sign, cutaneous hyperesthesia, convulsions, vomiting, slow pulse, etc.). However, the cerebrospinal fluid is transparent, and the pressure is increased. Tuberculous bacteria can be demonstrated in the cerebrospinal fluid.

Q: In addition to the symptoms described above, what other symptoms do miliary tuberculosis patients have?

A: Other symptoms that are unique to this disease are evidence of miliary tubercles on the fundus retina. The gastrointestinal tract is also impaired, with loss of appetite, vomiting, constipation, or diarrhea. Proteinuria is present in the urine. Tuberculous bacteria can be demonstrated in the blood.

Q: What are the clinical forms of this disease?

A: Roughly speaking, there are three types: meningeal type, pulmonary type, and typhoid type.

Q: How to diagnose acute miliary tuberculosis?

A: As long as it is determined from the past history whether there is tuberculosis, tachycardia, shortness of breath, cyanosis, neurological symptoms; and fundus examination to see if there is retinal tuberculosis rash. X-rays can be taken of the lungs to see if there are fine spots.

Q: What diseases should it be distinguished from?

A: It should be distinguished from typhoid fever, septicemia, acute pneumonia, meningitis, pulmonary tuberculosis, malaria, etc.

Q: What is the prognosis of this disease?

A: Absolutely grim. Death usually occurs within two or three weeks.

Q: Is there a treatment method?

A: There is simply no treatment to speak of. Only symptomatic use of drugs to alleviate the patient's pain or use of drugs to maintain heart strength, stop coughing, and relieve pain.

Common Sense of Hygiene for Ear, Nose, Throat, and Eye Diseases

— Tang Renjin

(90) Pupil

The normal pupil is in the center of the iris. Usually, the left and right are the same size and are perfectly round. If we try to shine light obliquely into the pupil area, it will appear black. If we try to shine light completely through it, it will appear red. Sometimes the left and right pupils are not regular; in medicine, this is called pupillary deformity. This type of deformity is often seen in posterior synechia following iritis, traumatic iris rupture, spinal cord tabes, and cerebral syphilis, etc. If a part of the iris is missing, the pupil can form a long oval shape. Generally, those with a defect in the upper part are often caused by iridectomy. Those in the lower part are often congenital iris defects.

The size of the pupil can be accurately measured with a Haab's pupillometer. Physiologically, it varies according to the intensity of the light, refractive state, adjustment action, convergence reaction, and age, etc. Usually, the pupils of young people are larger. The pupils of newborns and the elderly are smaller.

In physiological state, the diameter of the pupil is two to four millimeters. If the diameter of the left and right pupils differs by more than one millimeter, it is a pathological phenomenon. In medicine, this is called anisocoria. This is often encountered in refractive abnormalities, glaucoma, paralysis of the internal eye muscles, monocular visual impairment, and central nervous system disorders, etc.

A Brief Discussion of Pulmonary Tuberculosis (94)

— Hu Jiayan

How young people with a predisposition to tuberculosis should choose their occupations is also an important issue in prevention and deserves to be mentioned here. Common opinion is that since the body is already weak, the chosen occupation should be easy and require little labor, such as teachers, officials, and writers. This is completely wrong. Because these people generally have strict working hours and find it difficult to consider physical fatigue, or they are constantly working at their desks all day, and the opportunity to contact fresh air and sunlight is far less than those who work outdoors. Therefore, for these young people, it is better to choose outdoor work such as agriculture, horticulture, and forestry. Because at least, there are many opportunities to enjoy sunlight and air; this is beneficial for life and cannot be achieved by the former. Regarding the occupation of a doctor, because of a deep understanding of the relationship, many people also pay attention to this; in fact, doctors cannot be separated from patients every day, and the opportunity to induce the disease is the most, so it is certainly not very appropriate!

Finally, there is another question to be raised, that is, whether young people with tuberculosis are suitable for exercise? Our answer is: appropriate physical exercise is certainly permissible and is not without benefit. However, the vigorous exercises currently promoted in schools, such as wrestling, football, long-distance running, and boxing, can cause excessive fatigue, and as a result, latent tuberculosis can easily become progressive, and hemoptysis is even more common, so it is absolutely impossible to take risks and try them. This is a major issue in national education, and it is hoped that domestic educators will pay attention to this and not blindly encourage it. (The End)

Since this article has been published in journals, readers have repeatedly inquired about the date of publication or requested that it be printed as a single book in advance. The "Anti-Tuberculosis Magazine" has also reprinted it on a regular basis, and the kindness and affection are beyond expectations. However, the author has difficulties, with medical and teaching duties, and very little time to write, so it has been delayed until today to be able to complete the manuscript; it is now planned to revise the original text once and then send it to the printer, and it should be published in June at the latest. I would also like to take this opportunity to inform you of this. The author has not been able to reply to all the letters from you due to work, and I apologize for this.

Q&A on Dental Knowledge

— Lin Jianxian

Chapter 7: Treatment of Dental Diseases

Section 1: General Overview

(Question 159) Why should dental diseases be treated earlier than other diseases?

Answer: Most of the cells in our body have the ability to repair themselves, so ordinary diseases will gradually recover after a while. However, once a problem occurs with teeth, it will only get worse and worse, and there is little hope of natural repair. It must be treated and repaired artificially before the condition can be stopped. The later the treatment, the greater the loss and the more difficult the repair. Moreover, no matter how clever the artificial repair is, it is not as good as the natural one.

Advice to Students in Beiping Not to Demonstrate

— Special Correspondent

The Hebei-Chahar Political Council issued an order on the 3rd prohibiting student strikes, stating that according to past experience, strikes often occur at the time of the semester or when students are about to take exams. Students often use strikes to avoid exams. If students in various universities or other schools attempt to strike, they will be arrested or expelled. I am not very supportive of student demonstrations, but it is probably not true to say that students only want to avoid exams and use the opportunity to demonstrate. If they use the opportunity, there must be a reason to use it. It is the misfortune of the country that students have to use the opportunity to demonstrate. Although it is unavoidable that there are students who want to avoid exams by using the opportunity, I think these students are only a small minority.

However, since I do not approve of student demonstrations in fact, there is no need to discuss them in theory. Let me briefly mention two points: Student demonstrations are commonplace. Has there ever been a time when they did not end in a tragic result? As the saying goes, "Everyone is responsible for the rise and fall of the country." Patriotism is common to all. Precisely because patriotism is common to all, students do not need to demonstrate alone. Do students have patriotism while others do not? If we talk about responsibility, the government's responsibility is after all ten or a hundred times greater than the students' responsibility. Therefore, the government's patriotism should also be ten or a hundred times greater than that of the common people. Why should students seek trouble for themselves and do something that is beyond their duty? Students' responsibility lies in studying. If they do not succeed in their studies, it is the shame of the students. If the country wants to be rich and strong, it can only rely on science. If science does not progress, it is also the shame of the students. Whether the country is currently in turmoil and needs science to save the country, or in times of peace and prosperity, when there is no external disaster, it can only rely on science to strengthen itself. Therefore, students should now work ten or a hundred times harder than usual. Moreover, the current war is a war of science. No matter how students shout with their bare hands, it is not enough to help. Even if the whole country uses its strength to resist, it may not help the situation. Moreover, what kind of situation is North China in? Students are under such immense pressure that they have almost no room to breathe. Is there still a possibility of struggle?

Even so, we people who do not live outside the pass or in North China have seen few shocking things. Even if we do see them, it is only a glimpse in the newspaper or a story from a friend. It is still possible to say a few calm and sarcastic words while watching the fire from across the river, before it burns our eyebrows. If we were already in this kind of strange organization, I am afraid there would be no room for talk. Should the general public still demonstrate? Students! You should work hard in your studies and repay the country in the future.

Encounter

— Bai Ling

Once, my father took my mother, brother, and me back to our home from Jinan.

It was in the spring, and the weather was already warm. The mouth of the Yellow River, which had been frozen, began to melt under the caress of the sun.

To avoid the ravages of floods, my family had moved countless times, but no matter how we moved, we could not avoid being disturbed by the water. This time, we moved to a house on the back ridge not far from the river embankment.

Whenever spring came, people would be stirred by the indelible memories, and they would begin to live a life of worry and unease.

The yellow and turbid river water flowed like the open mouth of a man-eating demon, raging! Roaring! Plains, mountains, villages, and human figures had been washed away and swallowed by its flood waves several times!

Some people could save their lives from the disaster, but most of them became wanderers in other places, or they took the risk and became heroic bandits.

Not long after we lived at home, we encountered the river water rising again. So, my grandfather anxiously asked my father to take us away from home as soon as possible. But he stubbornly refused to go with us, and he was willing to stay at home. He said that when the water was high, he could find a way to run. He was a really stubborn old man. He had been a hardworking and loyal farmer all his life.

The next day, before dawn, my father took my mother, brother, and me on a journey. It was drizzling. My grandfather put us on the sedan car and walked with us for a while on the dark road. With a reluctant expression, he murmured in a prayerful tone: "I hope God will bless you and keep you safe on the road!"

Seeing my grandfather's unusual sadness, my father couldn't help but say, "I think we should go together. You don't have to stay at home alone."

My grandfather covered his lips with his hand and said hesitantly, "Don't worry about me..." Then, he walked back despondently.

On the road, our hearts felt inexplicably sad! When we arrived at Taiping Town, the sun was already red, and we were a little happy. After eating something on the road, we continued to walk.

Just as we arrived at Wangjiagou, the driver turned his head in panic and said to my father, "The front, the front, the front is not good, there is trouble ahead! I saw a car rolling over on the ground from a distance."

"Then, quickly, quickly, quickly turn back!" My mother was stunned.

"Or we can also walk south..." My father seemed to have some experience, and he glanced around.

My brother and I were so frightened that we almost cried.

The driver followed my father's instructions and changed direction, walking on a road to the south. But not far away, eight rough men jumped out of a ditch beside the road. They held wooden sticks in their hands and rushed towards us. "Stop! The car in front. Hand over the money quickly!" Some voices shouted excitedly.

My father was afraid that they would hurt us, so he hurriedly jumped out of the car and said tremblingly, "Brothers, we are poor travelers, and we don't have much money with us, just a few travel expenses..." As he spoke, he rummaged through the few old clothes bags placed in the car for them to see. Then, he took out a paper package from one of the clothes bags: "These few dollars..."

A person standing next to my father stared straight at him, and at the same time, my father was touched by his gaze and began to search him. The man looked embarrassed, smiled, and said to my father with a red face, "You, you, you don't recognize me!"

My father grunted and stared blankly.

The man said again, "I, I am Lao Liu from Dongzhuang, don't you remember? I used to work as a farmhand in your back neighborhood."

My father smiled, clapped his hands on his thighs and said, "Ah, I remember. I said Lao Liu, you, you are now..."

"I can't make a living now... In recent years, there have been floods, and there have been wars and chaos. Who would hire me as a farmhand again..."

So, my father held out a paper package in his hand and said, "I said, Lao Liu, we are all acquaintances, so, you take these few dollars and everyone have a pot of wine, okay?"

He pushed my father's hand away and said politely, "How can this be done? No need, no need, you are travelers, and you can't move a step without money!"

This unexpected panic allowed us to pass safely.

My father put the few dollars back into the clothes bag.

My mother looked at my father and said calmly, "Lao

Page 18

Liu wasn't a very honest person, was he? He has learned to be bad now!"

My father coughed a few times, as if he hadn't heard my mother's words. He was gazing at the wide, yellow, and turbid river in the distance.

Slaughterhouse

— Meng Hua

It was an early summer afternoon. I was returning from the Xishi Market in Tianqiao and wanted to walk towards Qianmen Street when, somehow, I lost my way and ran into an unknown alley. On both sides of the alley were some low and dilapidated houses. The white ash painted on the outside had faded completely, and the yellow mud, grass roots, and broken bricks were all exposed. I boldly walked past, but gradually I found such wooden signs and paper strips:

"Lanfang's place for business"

"Yueyuehong two maos at your service"

"Tianlu just arrived, Xiaoguixiang two maos at your service, guaranteed to satisfy you"

The latter paper strip was pasted outside a small house with peeling paint. At that time, the door was open, and behind the old red lacquer screen, I saw some naked women sitting around a square table in the courtyard. A young man was squatting under the screen, staring at me with fierce eyes. I was a little scared and hurriedly ran past.

This alley was only narrow, but not long. In front was a huge pile of garbage, and turning from there might be a main road, because I heard the sound of bicycle bells. Judging from the few houses I had passed, this was a place where low-class prostitutes gathered, because those wooden signs and paper strips were pasted on the walls of each house. But before I had reached the end, a middle-aged woman heard footsteps, jumped out of another house, saw me, and put on a smiling face! She greeted me, and then swayed her buttocks, making a gesture to seduce people to fall into depravity. Her upper body was naked, and she was wearing a pair of red shorts. "Come on! I'll make you happy!" she said, walking down. I ran past in a panic, my back felt like it had been poured with a burst of ice water, and my whole body trembled. Finally, like a deserter running dozens of miles, I didn't dare to look back and walked out of that alley.

This happened a while ago. But what made me aware of the inside story of this "at your service" was on an early autumn afternoon. This impression will undoubtedly not be forgotten at the moment of my death. It showed me another side of the hell in this world. The thing is like this:

I often went outside Xizhimen to visit a good friend of mine at a certain school. Every time I got off the tram and stepped over the base of Xizhimen city wall, the rickshaw pullers would surround me and shout:

"Pull you there, go to Shanghai Dian!"

"Go to Chengdashuxiao for two diao qian, want it?"

When I didn't answer them, those rickshaw pullers would change their smiling faces and yell:

"Going to Huangtukeng? Take my car, I guarantee you!"

"What kind of place is Huangtukeng?" When I met my friend, I asked him this, because I really found the rickshaw puller's words mysterious.

Although my friend had lived outside the city for a long time, he couldn't even answer this "famous" place. And when I told this question to the doorman in the dormitory, those doormen were unexpectedly surprised.

"What? What do you two ask this place for?"

But he finally couldn't resist us, and on a Sunday afternoon, the three of us finally went to Huangtukeng.

It was a narrow and dirty street, with dust flying on the street, and the dust was filled with an unknown stench. From the intersection at the west end of the street, turn right, and facing you is a row of small mud houses coated with yellow soil. Outside, two or three naked male beggars were catching lice, all with a tuft of thick black chest hair. They looked at us with strange eyes, and then discussed in a kind of incomprehensible secret language.

"Hey, there are guests on the east side, go to the third house on the west side, Shunxi is pretty good, just came from Luomahu in Tianjin." One of them stood up and pointed to the west and said to us.

My friend was already scared and wanted to go back. The two of us walked to the front of that house. A piece of paper was pasted in front of the rotten bamboo curtain, which read: "Shunxi four diao at your service." There was also a row of small characters next to Shunxi, which was no longer clear.

A person ran out of the next house, carrying a top in one hand, panting and walking towards the east. It was at this time that a man lifted the curtain for us and let us go in.

Facing us was a row of earth pits, with some weeds on top of the pits. On top of the weeds was a woman lying with her upper body naked, while the outer pit was a completely naked blind woman, moaning softly there. The room was very dim, and a strong stench hit my nose.

"Shunxi, have a customer!" The man shouted loudly.

Hearing this voice, the woman on the left didn't raise her head or open her eyes, just lifted the broken blanket covering her lower body. Presented before our eyes was a woman with a body covered in red rashes, and her ankles and joints were already ulcerated, her whole body stripped bare.

I completely fainted, unable to say a word, unable to walk a step. Only when the old doorman took out twenty copper coins did the woman slowly open her eyes. Suddenly, she sat up, holding the straw, and looked at me with fiery eyes, looking at the doorman who was with me. She unconsciously tore off a bunch of hair (her hair was already very sparse), and waved her hands hysterically, shouting, "Hey, get out, get out, this is not a place for you to come!"

She seemed to want to get out of bed. I hurriedly lifted the bamboo curtain and ran out. Then I heard a burst of fierce crying, mixed with the man's crude and barbaric curses. Immediately, those beggars squatting outside hurried to that house.

Because of this, I couldn't eat for three whole days. When will these slaughtered people be saved?

Mountain Goods Store

— Fang Zhou

In the early summer morning, the sun had not yet broken through the earth, and a pile of dark clouds was pushed up from behind the east mountain; then a dense drizzle sprinkled down from the clouds.

Old Man A-Cai poked his head out from the gap in the awning of the small boat, looked at the calm lake surface, and then suddenly drilled back into the cabin.

"I got up in the middle of the night to go to the stern of the boat to relieve myself, and when I saw the east opening, I knew today must be unreliable..." He muttered to himself, while reaching into the "dry pond" to search for his damp tobacco pipe.

"It looks like the boat won't be leaving today again! When you go to the teahouse, go to Wanyuan Three Line to ask." His wife was lighting the stove, because the wet firewood couldn't catch fire, so the smoke was billowing out; she kept her mouth close to the stove door blowing air, while wiping away her tears with one hand. Thinking that it was raining today, and the boat couldn't leave as expected, she stopped blowing air and said to her husband.

Old Man A-Cai, however, lit a piece of paper tinder and started patting the tobacco pipe on the stern of the boat, making "ba ah! ba ah!" sounds. He seemed not to have understood what his wife said.

The people on Xia Street in the town gradually became lively, and the stalls on Shedu Bridge were also set up one by one; the teahouse under the Qiaodun was already full of villagers, leisurely drinking tea, and talking loudly about the market prices of mountain goods and rural news. A few small grocery stores and a mountain goods store also took off their row of doors and were sorting out the various goods, or putting out the goods shelves in front of the door.

The villagers came to the street in groups of three or five, some wearing a broken palm-fiber hat and a worn-out straw raincoat, while others carried an umbrella. They came to inquire about the small plum market and buy things.

"Opening store boss, what's the market price for small plums today!" Genfu walked to the front of the store and asked the big-headed Wanyuan Three like this.

"The market hasn't come yet. It's raining today, I'm afraid there won't be any customers." He shook his round head without expression.

The rain wasn't heavy nor did it seem like it was going to stop, it just drifted, drifted; the humid and low-pressure climate was oppressively uncomfortable.

At breakfast time, the general villagers returned to their homes to eat one after another; so the streets slowly became quiet, —the teahouse only had empty board tables left, and the scabby-headed waiter was lonely cleaning up the empty teapots and teacups.

At noon, the market became lively again; the front of Wanyuan Three's store was already full of loads of round green plums, and many men and women waiting to sell were panting and squeezing in front of the store, constantly wiping the sweat from their foreheads with the corners of their clothes. However, the big scale in the store, although still hanging on the eaves like a dried dead fish as usual, didn't look like it was about to open. Only a few weighers and clerks were lying on the counter talking and laughing.

"Hasn't the scale opened yet?" Anxious Huang Guanbao rested his load of plums and squeezed into the crowd to ask everyone.

"No! I've been waiting for almost two hours." A-Huizi turned his head and said.

Load after load of small plums were brought in, and they had almost piled up into a small hill; however, the store still showed no sign of action, and time passed moment by moment, getting close to evening soon.

"Is the scale going to open today?" A woman, a little impatient from waiting, asked the clerk lying on the counter and laughing.

"Not necessarily!" The clerk only answered faintly, and then turned his head away.

Anxiety and depression were tightly enveloping them. They felt that there was no hope of opening the scale today.

Wanyuan Three held a water pipe and lay on the window of the building, puffing and smoking, he looked at the people crowding in front of the store; Xian Taiqing Salt Company asked him to collect one hundred loads of small plums, and he could take advantage of this opportunity with few customers to suppress the price. Anyway, the villagers were waiting to use the money, and waiting until the scale opened tomorrow, the price could drop by at least half—at most only one yuan per load. As for Xian Taiqing Salt Company, it had already been agreed to pay three and a half yuan per load including commission to collect the plums. Moreover, he could deduct another 10% commission from the "orchard households", and the scale would also have differences? Wouldn't that two hundred yuan or so be readily available? This was ultimately less laborious than earning the commission alone! He couldn't help but smile when he thought of this. He looked at those anxious faces below and puffed on the water pipe with even more vigor.

It was still raining, and the reed mat shed in front of the store door was also leaking a little, dripping on the people crowding in the shed.

"If we don't sell it today, it will turn yellow tomorrow, what should we do?" Someone said worriedly.

"If no one wants it, dump it in the ditch!" Another person answered angrily.

In the evening, the rain had stopped, but the streets were very muddy, and the store had closed its row of doors early. Those orchard households had no choice but to disappointedly carry the original load of plums back, keep them overnight, and come back to sell them tomorrow. The several row of goods boats in the Shedu Bridge port were also crowded there without missing one.

Opening Chapter "Woman Cries for Agarwood"

The autumn scene is fragrant with osmanthus in August. A passionate woman cries in her boudoir. Only to hear. The sound of insects chirping outside the window is incessant. The wind blows the purple bamboo, rustling and响. The iron horse rings on the eaves. Lower my head in secret. Thinking to myself. Thinking of the handsome and talented man in my mother's house. It has not been half a month since I got married into my husband's house. The maid sends a letter into my room. Saying that the talented man is sick in his gums. I am just offering incense in vain. Praying to the heavens and the city gods. Wishing him peace and happiness. It has not been a month since I got married into my husband's house. The maid sends a letter into my room. Saying that the talented man has died. Making me. Cry to death several times and come back to life. My husband asked me why I was sad. I only said that my stomach pain is the hardest to bear. I should have come to the spirit to mourn. Only because I am just a newlywed bride. Not attending the funeral to the mourning hall. I can only secretly wear three parts of mourning for you. I tied a piece of linen to my chest. I don't wear red and green clothes. Wearing two plain home clothes. A pair of arch shoes on linen. I asked the maid to buy a piece of agarwood. I carved the handsome face of the talented man. Carved him with a square scarf and double ribbons. White jade in the center emits light. Wearing a sea blue sauce yellow belt. Red satin shoes with black satin trim. It's hard for me to carve you. Pacing back and forth in the study. It's hard for me to carve you. Opening your mouth and calling me dear little sister. It's hard for me to carve you. Playing chess opposite each other and watching the West Chamber. It's hard for me to carve you. Several times urging and difficult to distinguish. Only because the bridal sedan arrived at the hall. I had to harden my scalp to say goodbye to the talented man. When I turned upstairs, I cried sadly. Idle people only gossip. Only saying that I can't get rid of my parents. Who knows. I can't get rid of the affectionate and righteous talented man. Talented man. I say that your mouth is for offering on the dressing table. In the evening. The blue gauze curtain is used as a ancestral hall. There are so many sad things in the world. Other people's sadness is sad. My sadness is hidden in my stomach.

Aftersounds

The Silver Moon Troupe arrived in Shanghai in April and has been performing Camille at the Tiansheng Stage. The main performers are Zhang Xianlin and Jia Qiuyun.

All the members of the Star Troupe have returned to Shanghai, except for Ma Loufen and dozens of dancers who have not yet come to Shanghai.

The Moonlight Society is organized by Mao Ruijia. It is said that it has expanded internally and is widely recruiting members.

The special issue of the Mei Hua Music Concert and Dance program continues to be given away. Attach four cents in postage (half a cent for one). The society at No. 16, Remy Road and Shunnan Lane will receive it.

Recently, the Moonlight Society won a great victory over the China Public School in a basketball game with a score of 28 to 21.

Movies

A Grim Ancient Temple in "The Bloody Case of a Newlywed"

As soon as it rains, the Yi Hua studio looks even more melancholic, especially these days, with a dilapidated and grim ancient temple standing there. However, the three large Buddha statues in the center show very amiable expressions. The fish oil lamps in front of the hall are flickering dimly. In the Cheat-proof Eternal Incense Burner, the smoke is always lingering, which is very evocative. However, when you look around again, terror will immediately grab your heartstrings. Not only do the huge Buddha statues around reveal fierce and terrible eyes and attitudes, but in the western corner, there are quietly lying five or six black and vermilion coffins. The eerie state is enough to make people feel chilly!

This is a large set in the new film "The Bloody Case of a Newlywed" (formerly "Father and Son Heroes") by Yi Hua Company, and it is fully enveloped in a terrifying and ghostly atmosphere.

The Story of Begonia Red

This story probably happened ten years ago!

"Begonia Red" is a woman who sings Ping opera. Because her husband is a good-for-nothing gambler, all the money she earns so hard is taken away by him to gamble. Later, even her own child was sold by her husband to others, and her old father died. "Begonia Red" herself was also taken by a warlord and imprisoned in the warlord's mansion. Later, after the revolutionary army arrived, she left the prison. It seems that the world has also changed, and everything is different. Everything in the past is over. After suffering so much, she was finally taken away by her own son. Thus, this woman who had wandered for many years finally found her home.

Jack Holt and Ames Strong Co-Star in "Tide of Anger"

Great Shanghai Screening

United Photoplay Service Tidbits

"The Lost Lamb," this work, after a very long production time and a large amount of capital, is Cai Chusheng's greatest success after "Song of the Fishermen," and it is also the most exquisite crop of United Photoplay Service this year.

"Go to Nature" is a film that fully represents [Yuan Muzhi's] style. "Wild Rose" and "The Road" are inferior to it.

After "Filial Piety," United Photoplay Service has another production of "Song of a Loving Mother." This ethical film develops the spirit of maternal love to the greatest extent.

In "Filial Piety," Zhang Yi plays a prodigal son who has awakened. In "Song of a Loving Mother," he plays a sacred worker, a kind son.

Li Lili worked very hard in "Go to Nature," and her acting skills are better than in any of her previous films.
